He is the hero of the play called Ratnawali and his life is the subject of several other compositions. **पूर्वोद्दिष्टां** mentioned before; see verse 28 **सौधीन्सङ्गप्रणय** etc. **श्रीविशालां-श्रियांविशालां**—rich in prosperity. **सुचरितफलेस्वल्पीभूते**— Reward of good course of life being too little to enjoy the heaven. i. e. persons who have passed virtuous life are supposed to be entitled to enjoy heaven for a period varying with their virtuous deeds and when this whole stock is exhauasted, they are again supposed to be thrown down on the earth. **शेषैःसुकृतैः**— By the remnant of their virtuous deeds. For the description of a city as a colony of heaven cf. R. 15. 29 **स्वर्गाभिष्यन्दवमनं कृत्वेवोपनिवेशिता.** Also Kumar 6,37 in the same words as **स्वर्गाभि** &c. applied to **आलका** there **यक्ष** supposes these men to be thrown down on the earth again before the whole stock of their merit was exhausted and consequently having a right to enjoy heaven for some period more, they as it were, brought down a piece of heaven on the earth for their sake, and that was this town Ujjayini consequently it must be surpassing all the towns on the earth. For Ujjayini vide note verse 28. **कान्तिमत्**-**कान्तिरस्या अस्तीति** possessing splendour. **विशाला** is another name of Ujjayini. For the similar description of Ujjayini, Shipra, and Mahakala. cf. Rugu. 6.32,34. **एक**—Matchless.

** Verse 31**. In this and the following four verses the poet gives the description of Ujjaini. **दीर्घीकुर्वन्** etc. All these adjectives are applicable to the breeze as well as to a lover. **दीर्घीकुर्वन् ** etc. in the case of a lover means causing the domestic birds by his fondling words to continue their sweet, indistinct and lusty warbling for a long time. **स्फुटित** etc— His person perfumed by the full blown lotuses crushed under their body. **अङ्गानुकूल—** agreeable to the limbs. In the case of a lover shampooing the body after close embrace. **भवभूति** has also said the same. **अशिथिलपरिरं भैर्दत्तसंवाहनानि** This poet has also elsewhere said, cf. 11.33 **सम्भोगान्ते मम समुचितो हस्तसंवाहनानाम्** cf. also sakuntal 3.18. **अङ्के निधायकरभोरुयथासुखन्तेसंवाहयामि चरणावुत पद्यताम्रौ. शिप्रा—** Name of a river which issues from the Sipra lake and on the bank of which stands Ujjayini. There is some propriety in using this word as it conveys an idea of coolnees. **प्रार्थनाचाटुकार–प्रार्थनासुचाटुकरोतीतिचाटुकारः** The object of using fond words is to make women forget of the previous languor and consent to the request of their lovers. cf. Raghu 6.14** प्रियः प्रियायाः प्रकरीति चाटुम्**.

** ** **Verse b*.*** **प्रसारितान्** is applicable to all the nouns **हारान् शङ्खशुक्तीः, मरकतमणीन्** and **गङ्गान्** with a change in the form according to the requirements. **तरलगुटिकान्तरल** the central gem of a necklace, and **गुटिका—** a round ball, i. e. a round jewel in the middle. **श्याम** means both dark and green. It is better to take it here to mean green. **उन्मयखप्ररोहान्—** shooting forth its rays. **तोयमात्रावशेषाः** etc**—** one might imagine that the oceans have only water remaining in them as all jewels in them have been taken out of them and brought in the city of Ujjayini.

** ** **Verse c***.* For the first line vide note verse 31.**किल** It is reported. **अभिज्ञ—** vide note verse 32. **कोविदज्ञानवृद्धान्—**This is **भाविकालङ्कार—** which is thus defined, **अतीतानागते यत्र प्रत्यक्षत्वेन लक्षिते॥ अत्यद्भूतार्थकथनाद्भाविकं तदुदाहतम्॥ प्रत्यक्षाइव यद्भावाः क्रियन्ते भाविनः। तद्भाविकम्**॥ i. e. it is a figure of speech which consists in describing the past or future so vividly that it appears to be actually present.

*** Verse d***. **वाहाः-वहन्तीतिवाहाः—** horses. The poet means that the horses here were equal to those of the sun both in colour and speed. The horses of the sun's chariot are supposed to be grey. **प्रभेदाद्वृष्टिमन्तः— **There is a constant flow of rut from the temples of elephants in a mad state **अग्रन्नयन्तीत्यग्रण्यः—**Those that lead the van, **प्रतिदशमुखं** standing face to face of Dashamukha. **प्रति, अभि** govern the accusative. **दशमुखः—**Ten-faced-one, another name of Ravana king of Lanka, killed by Rama the eighth incarnation of Vishnu. **चन्द्रहासव्रणाङ्कैः प्रत्यादिष्टाभरणरुचयः— **Chandruhasa was the name of Ravana's sword. Those warriors despised putting ornaments considering wounds received in a battle-field to be best ornaments of warriors and as they had received wounds from the weapon of so famous a warrior as Ravana, they were justly proud of them. This is also **भाविकालङ्कार** vide note verse c.

**Verse 32.** **केशसंस्कारधूपाः**-**संस्कारणां धूपाः संस्कारधूपाः संस्कार** is equal to **संस्कारद्रव्य— **dressing articles such as ointment and others applied at the time of decoration. cf. Sakuntala 7. 3. **यत्तेदृष्टमसंस्कारपाटलोष्ठपुटम्मुखम्** also. **स्वभावसुन्दरंवस्तु संस्कारनापेक्षते. बन्धुप्रीति-बन्धौ प्रीतिः— **Love for thee whom they regard as relativo cf. verse 49. **बन्धुप्रीत्यासमरविमुखोः**, &c. **पादरागः**-**लाक्षारसः— **reddye applied to the foot. In India women generally apply red-dye to the palm of their foot and while they walk before it is dried, foot-prints are impressed on the floor. **लक्ष्मीः** is equal to general prosperity as well as splendour.

**Verse 33**. **भर्तुःकण्डच्छगिरीति—** This alludes to the drinking of poison by Śiva and when the ocean was churned by the gods and demons, fourteen articles are said to have been churned from it, out of which poison was one. Its horrible effects were seen just aftter its appearance on the earth and every one became afraid of it. This God was requested by other gods and he is said to have drunk it. Since that time his throat acquired dark-blue colour and he is called Nilakantha. It is said that to cool down the effect of this poison he has ever since placed the moon and the Ganges over his head. **गणैः—** There were several species of demi-gods in attendance of Śiva. They were under special superintendance of Ganeśa who is in consequence called **गणपति** compare **गणनान्न्वा गणपतिं हवामहे कविं कवीनाम्** &c. **सादरंवीक्ष्यमाणः.** They would naturally have curiosity to look at thee who shalt have the colour of their master's throat. **आदर** may mean the mingled feelings of curiosity and respect. **त्रिभुवनगुरुः-त्रयाणाम्भुवनानांसमाहारःत्रिभुवनं** **तस्य गुरुःस्वामी—** master of heaven, earth and hell. **चण्डी** is another name of **पार्वती** the wife of **शङ्करः**, This name she must probably have got when she assumed the fierce form to kill the demon **महिषासुर** for **चणु** means fierce. **धाम**-**महाकाल**. This was regarded as the most sacred place on earth as giving not only salvation but also any wordly desire by visiting it as **आकाशे तारकं लिङ्गं पाताले हाटकेश्वरं मर्त्यलोके महाकालं दृष्ट्वा कामतिमाप्नुयात्** The poet's attachment for **महाकाल** appears very strong as the description given in 34, 35, 36 is a very striking one **गन्धवत्याः— **The poet has mentioned **क्षिप्रा** in verse 32 and here he makes mention of **गन्धवती,** but there are not two rivers in the vicinity of Ujjayini. So these two must be the same. **तोयक्रीडा** or **जलक्रीडा** was it appears prevalent in ancient times among royal and other wealthy families as this and other poets make frequent mention of it every now and then. It must have consisted of going into waters of rivers, lakes etc with lovers and throwing waters on each other; at this time they must be applying perfumes to the body. **तिक्त— **bitter as well as fragrant; here it must be taken in the latter sense.

** ** **Verse 34**. **अन्यस्मिन् काले— **At any other time than evening. **ते स्थातव्यं** for **ते** instead of **त्वया** vide note verse 4. **नयनविषयमत्येति**-**अस्तङ्गच्छति** sets. **पटहताङ्कृ— **serving the purpose of a drum. **शूलिन्— **possesser of **शूल— **a sharp-pointed weapon, the insignia of Siva. **आमन्द्रम्-** **आ** prefixed to adjectives and sometimes to nouns has a dimunitive sense, as **आपाण्डुर, आकम्प.** **गर्जितानामविकलं फलं लप्स्यसे— **Thou wilt have occasion to turn thy thundering to a good use, as being useful at Siva's worship. Verse 35. **पादन्यास** etc.**— **stepping of the foot at the time of dancing at evening-worship. There is yet in vogue the custom of concubine's dancing at the evening worship of Shiva in some famous temples of Shiva. All festival occasions are accompanied by this sort of dancing **रत्नछाया ** etc**— **The luster of the jewels worn on these women's hands, will enter the cavities of the handle which in consequence will appear as if set with the lustre. **चामरैःक्लान्तहस्ता**— one of those women's duties is to fau the God by chauries, consequently their hands will be tired by fanning. Mallinatha takes it to mean, tired on account of holding chauries in hand at the time of dancing; this being one of the varieties of dancing. **देशिकं** dance, which is thus defined **खड्गकन्दुकवस्त्रादिदण्डिकाचामरस्रजः। वीणां च धृत्वा यत्कुर्युर्नृत्यन्तद्देशिकं भवेदिति॥** When concubines hold any of these things in hands at the time of dancing, it is called **देशिक** dance. **नखपदसुखान्**— Nail marks received from their paramours. The rain-drops shall produce cooling effect on these marks and consequently will be agreeable **कटाक्षानामोक्ष्यन्ते**— will cast sidelong glances to return the obligation they receive from thee. The glance from women is a sort of blessing that shall be the return for thy favour of pouring water-drops on their wounds. Here **यक्ष** also implies that the cloud might immediately obtain the fruit of visiting that holy place in the shape of women's glances and that he shall not have to wait for it till next life or any future period.

** ** **Verse 36**. **पश्चात्**— After the evening worship. **नृत्यारम्भे-नृत्य-ताण्डवनृत्य**— a kind of dance which Śiva himself is supposed to make in the evening after the evening worship, **सान्ध्यम्**-**सन्ध्यायाम्भवंसान्ध्यम्**— pertaining to the evening. **उच्चैर्भुजतरुवनम्मण्डलेनाभिलीनः**— fitting the circle of his arm which resembled the forest lofty trees. For this comp. **गजासुरमर्दनान्तरं भगवान्महादेवस्तदीयमाद्राजिनं भुजमण्डलेन बिभ्रत्ताण्डवं चकारेति प्रसिद्धिः**। i. e. after killing **गजासुर** Śiva taking his hide wet with blood in the circle of his arms made the **ताण्डव** dance. **आर्द्रनागाजिनेच्छाम्**—The hide of the **नागासुर** wet, of course with blood **हर पशुपतेः** &c.-Remove his longing ** ** &c. by being a substitute in its place. **शान्तोद्वेग**— Her fears subsided on account of thy taking the place of the hide of the elephant. This shows that Parvati must have been looking with terror upon the hide of the elephant and consequently when that fear of hers would be removed she would look at the devotion with a steady—eye. **भक्ति**— Devotion, love for the respected **भवानी** wife of **भव** (Śiva) **इन्द्रवरुणभवशर्वरुद्रमृडहिमारण्ययवयवनमातुलाचार्याणामानुगागमः स्यात्ङीश्च.** These words take **आनी **to form their fem.

** Verse 37**. **योषित्— अभिसारिका**— a woman who either goes to meet her lover or keeps an appointment made by him. **सूचिभेद्य**—To be pierced by a needle, hence thick, pitchy. **आलोक**—sight.cf. Verse 3. also Sakuntal. 1. 9. **यदालोकेसूक्ष्मं** &c. **निकष**— line on the test stone. **स्निग्ध—**Lustre. **तोयत्सर्गस्तनिमुखर**-**तोयत्सर्गस्तनित**— may be dissolved in either way, either as **द्वन्द्व** or **सप्तमीतत्पुरुष** as **तोयोत्सर्गश्चस्तनितं च, तोयोत्सर्गस्तनिते** or **तोयोत्सर्गेस्तनितं**— but the former way of dissolving it is better as each separately is undesirable. The only objection to dissolve it as **द्वन्द्व** is that the members of **द्वन्द्व** must be so arranged as to have the words having few vowels first. But that rule not being very strictly observed, as we have **लक्षणहेतु** as **द्वन्द्व** with less vowels in the second member. It is better to take in the first way. **विक्लवाः** may be taken as **स्वभावभीताः**— Naturally timid.

 **Verse 38. सुप्तपारावतायाम्**—shows freedom from disturbance. **यक्ष** means to say that the cloud shall have undisturbed rest there on account of the calm and quiet state of the place. cf. Vikram. 3. 2. **धूपैः सन्दिग्धपारावतावडभयः** also Malavi. 2. 13. **वलभिपरिचयद्वेषिपारावतानिसौधानि.** **विलसन** has double meaning, 'Flashing or sporting.' as applied to **विद्युत्** it means flashing and as applied to **बल्लभ** it means sporting. "On account of the long sporting (in the shape of flashing) with thee her husband" **दृष्टे सूर्ये** Loc. absolute **मन्दायन्ते** &c**. अर्थन्तरन्यास** Vide note Verse 3. **मन्दायन्ते**—Denominative from **मन्द अभ्युपेतार्थकृत्य–कृत्य** here means execution and **अर्थ**—business.

** Verse 39**. **खण्डिता**—A woman crossed in love. One of the 8 principal heroines of Hindu dramas cf. note on **योषित** Verse 37. She is thus defined, **पार्श्वमेति प्रियो यस्या अन्यसम्भोगचिन्हितः। सा खण्डितेति कथिता धीरैरीर्ष्याकषायिता**॥ That woman disturbed by jealousy who is followed by husband with marks of having enjoyed another women is called **खण्डिता** **शान्तिनेतव्यं—**is to be dried. These women on account of their husband's disregard for them shall have passed the night in shedding tears and those tears shall have to be dried by their husbands in the morning. **प्रालेयास्रै** etc.**नलिनी** is considered the wife of the sun, she too on account of her husband's absence at night shall be crossed in love and shall be shedding tears in the form of dew which shall have to be dried by her huse band, the sun with his hand (rays). **कर** has a double meaning 'hand and rays’. **त्वयि**, **कररुधि** Loc abs. When thou wilt obstruct (come in the way of his hands (rays) **अनल्पाम्यसूयः स्यात्**—Will not be a little angry i.e. on account of thy coming in the way of his love c.f. Rughu. 6.74 **शुक्राभ्यसूयाविनिवृत्तये यः** also. Rughu 7, 2 **रूपेषवेशेषुचसाभ्यसूया** and 9, 64, Kumar 3.

** Verse 40**. **गम्भीरा** by this the noble heroine is indirectly alluded to. **प्रसन्ने** qualifies both **चेतसि** and **पयसि** in the case of former it means pure on account of being free from sinful thoughts and in the case of the latter clear, i. e. free from turbid matter. c.f. M. 3. 9, **गङ्गां शरन्नयति सिन्धुपतिं प्रसन्नां.** also Kumar 7.74 **प्रसन्नचेत्तः सलिलः शिवोऽभून्.** and sakuntula 5–21. **कूलङ्कषेवसिन्धुः प्रसन्नमम्भस्तटञ्च.** **छायात्मापि** etc. Though thou wilt not personally enter still thy reflected body will necessarily do as both being transparent **मोद्यीकर्तुं**—And as entering its water is to be a matter of necessity to thee, thou wilt not disappoint her by thy indifference.

** Verse 41**. The river here being compared to a woman, on the point of having sexual intercourse with her husband, every epithet is applicable to both the river and the woman. **लम्बमानम्य** in the case of the cloud, ‘hanging down' for taking in water; in the case of a lover, (sleeping) resting on the hip of his beloved. The fourth line is **अर्थान्तरन्यास** vide note verse 3. **कोविजहातुंसमर्थः**—Question of appeal. The answer being 'no one etc'. to take in the first way. **विक्लवाः** may be taken as **स्वभावभीताः**— Naturally timid.

** Verse 38.** **सुप्तपारावतायाम्—** shows freedom from disturbance. **यक्ष** means to say that the cloud shall have undisturbed rest there on account of the calm and quiet state of the place. cf. Vikram. 3. 2. **धूपैः** **सन्दिग्धपारावतावडभयः** also Malavi. 2. 13. **वलभिपरिचयद्वेषिपारावतानिसौधानि. विलसन** has double meaning, ‘Flashing or sporting.’ as applied to **विद्युत्** it means flashing and as applied to **वल्लभ** it means sporting. "On account of the long sporting (in the shape of flashing) with thee her husband” **दृष्टे सूर्ये** Loc. absolute **मन्दायन्ते** &c. **अर्थान्तरन्यास** Vide note Verse 3. **मन्दायन्ते**— Denominative from **मन्द. अभ्युपेतार्थकृत्य—कृत्य** here means execution and **अर्थ—**business.

 **Verse 39.** **खण्डिता—** A woman crossed in love. One of the 8 principal heroines of Hindu dramas cf. note on **योषित** Verse 37. She is thus defined, **पार्श्वमेति प्रियो यस्या अन्यसम्भोगचिन्हितः। सा खण्डितोति कथिता धीरैरीर्ष्काषायिता॥** That woman disturbed by jealousy who is followed by husband with marks of having enjoyed another women is called **खण्डिता** **शान्तिनेतव्यं** is to be dried. These women account of their husband's disregard for them shall have passed the night in shedding tears and those tears shall have to be dried by their husbands in the morning. **प्रालेयांस्रै** etc. **—नलिनी** is considered tho wife of the sun, she too on account of her husband's absence at night shall be crossed in love and shall be shedding tears in the form of dew which shall have to be dried by her huse band, the sun with his hand (rays). **कर** has a double meaning ‘hand and rays’. **त्वयि, कररुधि** Loc. abs. When thou wilt obstruct (come in the way of his hands (rays) **अनल्पाम्यसूयः स्यात्—** Will not be a little angry i.e. on account of thy coming in the way of his love c.f. Rughu. 6.74 **शुक्राभ्यसूयाविनिवृत्तये यः** also. Rughu 7,2 **रूपेषुवेशेषुचसाभ्यसूया** and 9, 64, Kumar 3.

** Verse 40.** **गम्भीरा** by this the noble heroine is indirectly alluded to. **प्रसन्ने** qualifies both **चेतसि** and **पयसि** in the case of former it means pure on account of being free from sinful thoughts and in the case of the latter clear,i. e. free from turbid matter. c. M. 3. 9, **गङ्गां शरन्नयति सिन्धुपतिं प्रसन्नां.** also Kumar 7.74 **प्रसन्नचेत्तः सलिलः शिवोऽभूत्** and sakuntula 5—21. **कूलङ्कषेवसिन्धुः प्रसन्नमम्भस्तटञ्च. छायान्मापि** etc. Though thou wilt not personally enter still thy reflected body will necessarily do as both being transparent **मोद्यीकर्तुं—**And as entering its water is to be a matter of necessity to thee, thou wilt not disappoint her by thy indifference.

** Verse 41.** The river here being compared to a woman, on the point of having sexual intercourse with her husband, every epithet is applicable to both the river and the woman. **लम्बमानस्य** in the case of the cloud, ‘hanging down’ for taking in water; in the case of a lover, (sleeping) resting on the hip of his beloved. The fourth line is **अर्थान्तरन्यास** vide note verse 3. **कोविजहातुंसमर्थः**— Question of appeal. The answer being 'no one etc'.

** Verse 42**, It is a well-known fact that the earth smells as well as exhales a sort of good smell just after the first fall of rain when it is quite dry by the sun. **स्रोतस्** is used in a peculiar sense of 'nose' here **स्रोतोरन्ध्र**— Nostrils. **देवपूर्वगिरिं**— a mode of expression peculiar to the author. To **गिरि** having for its first syllable **देव** i. e. **देवगिरि** to mountain **उदुम्बर**— A kind of fig tree whose leaves and sticks are mostly used for religious purposes. **नीचैर्वास्यति**— will gently fan thee.

** Verse 43.** **स्कन्द,** he was also called Kartikeya by his being reared by six Krittikas. He is the Mars, or the god of war of the Indian mythology. He is the son of Siva, (but born without the direct intervention of a woman). Most of his epithets have reference to the circumstance of his birth. Siva cast his seed into Agni who had gone to the god in the form of a dove while he was enjoying Parvati's company. He being unable to bear it cast it into the Ganges. It was then transferred to six Krittikas, when they went to bathe in the Ganges. Each of whom therefore conceived and brought forth a son. But these six sons were then mysteriously combined into one of extraordinary form with six heads, twelve hands and eyes. According to some the seed was thrown into the thicket of reeds hence his names He is said to Sharavanabhava, Sharajanman." have pierced the Krauncha mountain, hence his name Kraunchadarana. He was the commander of the army of gods in their war with Taraka, a powerful demon whom he vanquished and slew, hence his name Senani, Tarakajit, He is represented as riding a peacock. After killing the demon he is supposed to have fixed his abode on Devagiri at the request of gods. for his birth compare Rughu 2.75, **सुरसरिदिवतेजोवन्हिनिष्ठ्युतमैशम्,** also Kumar 9. 13,14 **प्रसश्नचेता मदनान्तकारः, सतारकारेर्जयिनोभवाय॥ शक्रस्य सेनाधिपतेर्जयाय, व्यचिन्तयच्चेतसि भाविर्किञ्चित्॥ युगान्तकालाग्निमिवाविषह्यं, परिच्युतं मन्मथरङ्गभङ्गात्॥ रतान्तरेतः सहिरण्यरेतस्ययोर्ध्वरेतास्तदमोघमधात्॥ नियतववसतिं**— **नियता वसतिर्यस्य॥ पुष्पमेघीकृतात्मा**—changing thy watery form to that of flowery one in consequence of thy power to assume any form at will, vide verse C. **वासवीनां वासवस्येयं वासवी** pertaining to **वासव** (another name of Indra) because Indra is the lord of the army of gods, he being the ruler of heavens. **अन्यादिन्य—अतिक्रान्तमादित्यं**— surpassing the sun. **रक्षाहेतोः** etc, these two lines will be clearly understood from the note above on Skanda c.f. Rughu. 7.1, **स्कन्देनयुक्तांसाक्षाद्वेवसेनामिव**. The army of Inddra was to be protected from the violence of the demon Taraka, and with this object Siva put this semen virile into the mouth of the fire-god.

** Verse 41.** **ज्योतिर्लेखावलि**— having various colours in circular vikram 4.4 **विद्युल्लेखा- कनकरुचिरं** etc. **कुवलयदप्रापि** may be an adverb, or an adjective qualifying **कर्णे.** In the former case it would mean **कुवलयदलन्तत्प्रापिययातथा— **wears on the ear so as to make it in union with lotus-leaf; i. e. wears it with lotus-leaf. In the latter case it would mean **कुवलयदलार्हे** wears on the car fit for (or accustomed to) a lotus leaf. i. e. wears feathers on the ear instead of a lotus leaf. There is another reading **कुवलयदलक्षेपि** which means? the ear disregarding the lotus leaf which would be better taking her parental fondness into consideration. **हरशिरश्चन्द्रिका— **Siva always bears the crescent moon on his head to allay the afflicting pain caused by his taking into his stomach the deadly poison (**काल्कुट**) when it came along with wonderful things from the sea when it was churned by the gods and demons.
**पावकेः** vide note on **स्कन्द** verse 43. **अद्रिग्रहण— **by its echo from the mountain. (**ग्रहण—**echo).

** Verse 45.** **शरवणभव— **born in the thickǝt of reads. For Skanda's birth vide note verse 43. **वन** when compounded with the words **प्र, निः, अन्तः, शर, इक्षु, प्लक्ष, आम्र, कार्ष्य, खदिर, पीयूक्षा** becomes **वण—विणिन्** lute-player. **विणिभिः** etc.— The Shidhas will be away from thy path for fear of their lutes being spoiled by the drops of rain. **ऊल्लन्धिताध्वा**— Having gone a little further. **सुरभितनया**—(**सुरभि** is the name of a fabulous celestial cow supposed to yield disired object,) its daughter—cow in general. **आलम्भ**— Killing especially at the time of sacrifice. **स्रोतोमूर्त्या परिणतां**—Transformed into & stream, assuming the shape of a stream. cf. vikram. 4.28, **नदीभावेनेयं- ध्रुवमसहनासापरिणता. रन्तिदेव**—The name of the king of Dashapura. He belonged to the lunar race and was sixth in descent from Bharata. He possessed enormous riches, but he spent them in performing grand sacrifices. So great was the number of animals slaughtered during his reign both in sacrifices as well as for use in his kitchen that a river of blood is supposed to have issued from their hides, which was afterwards, appropriately called **चर्मण्वती. कीर्ति भुवि स्रोतोमूर्त्यपरिणतां**—which is none else but the fame of Rantideva thathas assumed the form of a stream on the earth. The name of this river is **चर्मण्वती.** See note on **रन्तिदेव**.

** Verse 46.** The view as seen by the celestial beings at the time of clouds bending down on the river is described here. It would appear to them like a continuous string of pearls having a supphire in the middle on the neck of the earth. **गगनगतयः**—Those that could move in the aerial space. **एकं**—continuous, unbroken.

** Verse 47.** **परिचित**—Developed. cf. Rughu. 3.24. **तत्प्रेमपरस्परस्योपरिपर्यचीयत**. But tho ordinary meaning ‘Familiar' would also suit here though this gives a better sense. **कृष्णशाराः**—**कृष्णाश्चशाराश्च**—Black-antilopes. **कुन्दक्षेपानुगमधुकरश्रीमुषाम्**—The comparison here is very exact, and beautiful, eye balls are compared to bees and the eye to **कुन्द** flowers. As the bee following the Kunda flowers tossed by the wind to and fro appears charming as sitting in the middle part of the flower so by the tossing up of the eye-lash the eyeballs in the middle of the eye appear beautiful. **कुन्द** flower appears to be a very favourite one with our poet he makes mention of it in this poem in several places. cf. II. 2, 50, also Sakuntal. 5.19, for similar idea. **भ्रमरइव विभाते नच खलुपरिभोक्तुं नैव शक्नोमि हातुम्. आत्मबिम्बम्**—They form, **पात्रीकुर्वन्**—Making an object. **दशपुर**—North of Avanti on river **चर्मण्वति** perhaps the modern Dholapur—**वधु**—woman in general, it also means a young woman, a daughter-in-law and a wife,

** Verse 48.** **ब्रह्मावर्त**—The region between the two celestial rivers **सरस्वती** and **दृषद्वती** north-west of Hastinapura. **छाया**—Shadowy form. **क्षत्रप्रधनपिशुनं**—Indicative of the battle of heroes. **प्रधन**—means either battle or destruction in the battle, we might either take it to mean 'the destruction of heroes or the battle of heroes. cf. Sisupal. 1. 75. **शत्रूणामनिशंविनाशपिशुनः**, also, Rugha 1.53 **अभ्युत्थानाग्निपिशुनैः**, Vikram 2 14 **तुल्यानुरागपिशुनं. कुरूणामिदं** **कौरवं**—Belonging to Kurus, here Kurus means both the Kauravas, and the Pandavas. **गाण्डीव** was the particular bow of Arjuna. **कुरुक्षेत्र**— An extensive plain near Delhi, the scene of the great war between the Kauravas and the Pandavas (**कुरु**—is the name of a country situated in the north of India about the modern sight of Delhi).

** Verse 49.** **रेवतीलोचनाङ्काम्**—Rewati was his wife and **अङ्क**—marked with the sign; hence resembling. cf. II. 23. **मद्गोत्राङ्कगेय.** Wine is always compared to the eyes of women by Sanskrit poets by their having common quality of fascinating the hearts of men, and the mention of Rewati is for the purpose of making it more fascinating as the eyes of one's own beloved are more attractive than those of other women **बन्धुप्रीत्यासमराबिमुखः**—Returning from the battle through his love for both parties. Balarama dit not take part in the war between the Kauravas and the Pandavas, and the poet attributes this circumstance to his love for either parties and not to his cowardice. cf. 32. **बन्धुप्रीत्याभवनशिखिभिः** etc. **अभिगम**—Lit; approach, hence enjoying. **लाङ्गली**—Aploughbearer, another name of Balarama, the elder brother of Krishna. He was the seventh son of Vasudeva & Devaki but was transferred to the womb of Rohini to save him from the cruelty of Kamsa. He and his brother Krishna were brough-up by Nanda in Gokula. He was very powerful and he was attached to the Kauravas, as Krishna to the Pandavas, but in the great Bharatiya war, he sided with neither party. He is represented as dressed in blue clothes (Vide Supra, Verse 64.)

** Verse 54.** **कनखलं**—Name of a sacred place and the hills
adjoining it near Gangadwara cf. **तीर्थ कनखलं नाम गङ्गाद्वारेऽस्ति॥** **शैलराज**—Lord of mountains (is the Himalayas). **जन्हु**—Name of an ancient king, son of Suhotra, who adopted the river Ganges as his daughter. The river Ganges when brought down from heaven by the austerities of Bhagiratha, was forced to flow over earth, to follow him to lowor regions. In its course it inundated the sacrificial ground of king Jahnu who being angry drank up its waters. But the gods and sages and particularly Bhagiratha appeased his anger and he consented to discharge those waters from his cars. Hence the the river is regarded as his daughter and is styled **जान्हवी, जन्दुकन्या**-**तनया-सुता, नन्दिनी** &c. cf, Raghuvams'a Sarga 8, śloka 95. **सगरतनयस्वर्गसीपानपङ्क्ति-सगर** was the name of a king of solar race. He was a son of Bahu and was called Sagara, because he was born together with gara (poison) given to his mother by the other wife of his father. By his wife Sumati, he had 60000 sons. He successfully performed 99 sacrifices, but when he commenced the hundredth, his sacrificial horse was stolen away by Indra, because success there in would have given the king the seat of Indra and Indra would have been displaced and carried down to Patala. Sagara thereupon commanded his 60,000 sons to search it out. Finding no trace of the animal on earth, they began to dig down towards Patala and in doing this they naturally increased the boundaries of the Ocean which was therefore called Sagara, cf. Raghuvamśa 13 **सर्ग**, 3 **श्लो.** **गुरीर्यियक्षोः कपिलेनमेध्ये रसातलं सङ्क्रमितेतुरङ्गे। तदर्थमुर्वीमवदारयाद्भेः पूर्वैःकिलायम्परिर्वीधतोनः॥** meeting with the sage Kapila, they rashly acused him of having stolen their horse, as a punishment for which they were instantly reduced to ashes by that sage. It was after several thousands of years that Bhagiratha succeeded in bringing down to the Patala, the celestial Ganges to water and purify their ashes and thus to convey their souls to heaven, hence the Ganges was as it were the flight of stairs for their souls to ascend Heaven. **गौरीवक्रभ्रुकुटिरचनां** (**भ्रुकुटिरचना**—wrinkles over the eye-brows) frowns on the face of Gauri, out of jealousy towards her cowife. **केशग्रहणमकरोत्** &c. who as it were cowed down her husband by her pulling him by the hair with her hand in the shape of waves. cf. Venisamhar 8. 11. 29. **केशग्रहः खलुतदादुपदात्म जायाः** also Kadambari 8. **यत्र रतेषुकेशग्रहाः**. It is said that the Ganges would not come down on the earth, on the ground that no one could bear her force while falling down. Then Śiva consenting to bear it, she fell on his head from heaven; thence issued fourth through the mountain Himalayas on the earth and then went to the Patala, cf. Bhartrahari. 3 44. **शिरः शार्वं स्वर्गात्.**

** Verse 51.** **व्योम्नि पूर्वाद्धेलम्बी**—hanging down in the sky by the hinder half and the fore half touching the river to take in the water. **अस्थानीपगत** etc.—The water of the Yamuna is black while that of the Ganges is white, consequently the Ganges when it unites with the Yamuna at Allahbad, acquires a sort of beauty by the admixture of these colours. The poet means to say that the Ganges will acquire the same beauty by the dark shadow in it, only difference being that of place which shall not be Allahbad in this case. This appears to be the poet's very favourite idea, cf. Kughu 6.48 **कलिन्दकन्यामथुरां गतापि गङ्गोमिसंसक्तजलैवभा ते.**

** Verse 52.** From 52—56 the poet gives the beautiful description of the Himalayas, which appears to be his special province. cf. Kumar 1.1—17; **आसीन** is irregular Pr. P. from **आस** to sit, by **मृग** is meant **कस्तूरिकामृग**—musk-deer, otherwise the production of musk being impossible. **नाभि**—musk, **प्रभव–प्रभवन्त्यस्मादिति प्रभव**—any object from which a thing springs up hence source. **विनयनविनीयतेऽनेनोति विनयन**—The remover cf. Rughu. 6,51 **अध्यास्य चाम्भः पृषतोक्षितानि शैलेयगन्धीनिशिलातलानि.**

** Verse 53.** **सरल**—A kind of pine-tree. **चमरी**—a wild cow whose tail is used as a fan cf. Kumarasambhava 13, cf. Kumar 1.9. **विघट्टितानां सरलद्रमाणाम्. बालब्यजनैश्चमर्यगिरिराजशब्दमर्थयुक्तङ्कुर्वन्ति** also Sisupalavadha 4—60. **बालभार**—Tail collected in a bunch. **आपर्न्नातिप्रशमनफलाः–आपन्नानामार्तिप्रशमनमेव फलं यासान्ताः**. Having for the fruit the allaying of the affliction of the distressed. The fourth line is **अर्थान्तरन्यास** vide note verse 3.

** Verse 54**. **शरभ**—A fabulous animal said to have 8 legs and to be stronger than a lion. **स्वाङ्गभङ्गाय लन्धयेयुः**—might jump and the result of which shall be only the mutilation of their limbs. **तुमुल**—abundant. The word **करक** is used both in mas, and neu. and **कारक** in fem. in the same sense. **केवा** etc is **अर्थान्तरन्यास** vide note verse 3. **केवा** is also a question of appeal, the answer being ‘all' such are the objects of contempt.’

** Verse 55.** **सिद्धः**—Asemi-divine being supposed to be of great purity and holiness and said to be particularly characterized by eight supernatural qualities called Siddhis, it also means inspired sages, the latter meaning is preferable here. **करण**—means ‘limbs as well as 'body,' here the latter meaning is to be taken. Ganas-vide note on verse 37. **प्राप्तये कल्पिष्यन्ते**—will be fit or adequate to; words having the sense of **पर्याप्ति** (fitness, sufficiency &c.) govern the dative. cf. Sakuntala 5—8 **कल्पसे रक्षणाय** also Vikram 3.1 **पश्चात्पुत्रैरपहृतभरः** **कल्पतेविश्रमाय**. and Kumar, 5.44. **विभावरीयद्यरुणाय कल्पते**.

** Verse 56**. **कीचक**—A species of bamboo. **मधुर**—agreebly to the ear; **संसक्त**—In harmony with (the sound produced from the bamboo). There is also another reading **संरक्ताभिः**—which would mean 'having sweet voice.' **त्रिपुरं–त्रयाणांसमाहारस्त्रिपुरं**—Three cities of gold, silver and iron in the sky air and earth built for demons by Maya, (These cities were burnt down along with the demons inhabiting them by Siva at the request of gods) when masculine it also means the demon presiding over these cities cf. Kumarasambhava. 7.48. **प्रवीणैः सङ्गीयमानत्रिपुरावदानोऽध्वानं ततार. सङ्गीतसम्यक्गीतं सङ्गीतं— **consert, music. **अर्थ— **materials, apparatus. i. e. thy sound will complete the apparatus of consert.

** Verse 57**. **उपतटम्–तटस्यसमीपे उपतटम्**—adverbial compound. **हंसद्वार—**Entrance or gate for geese going to the lake Manasa, vide note on verse 11. for it is supposed that the geese on their way pass on through this entrance. **भृगुपति–भृगु** is the name of a sage or it is another name of Jamadagni, and **भृगुपति** is the name of Paraśurama, a celebrated Brahmana warrior son of Jamadagni and the sixth incarnation of Vishnu, while young, he cut off the head of his mother Renuka at the command of his father when none of his other brothers were willing to do so. Some time after this, the king Kartavirya went to the bermitage of his father in his absenco and carried off his cow, on returning home Paraśurama fought with the king and killed him. His sons on hearing this became very angry and repaired to the hermitage and finding Jamadagni alone they shot him dead when Paraśurama, who was not then also at home, returned, he became very much exasperated and made the dreadful vow of exterminating the whole Khatriya race. He succeeded in fulfilling this vow and is said to have ‘rid the earth thrice-seven times of the royal race', He was afterwards, defeated by Rama, son of Daśaratha, though quite a boy of sixteen. (See Raghuvamśa 11. 68—91). He is said to have at one time pierced through the Kraunch mountain being jealous of the might of Kartikeya. cf. Gitagovinda, I. **क्षत्रियरुधिरमये जगदपगतपापं स्नपयति पयसि शमितभवतापम्। केशवधृतभृगुपतिरूप जय जगदीशहरे॥** He is one of the seven Chiranjivins practising penance on the Mahendra mountain. **क्रौऽच**—The name of a mountain supposed to be the grandson of Himalaya and said to have been pierced by Kartikeya and Paraśurama. **भृगुपतियशोवर्त्म**—As Paraśurama is supposed to have pierced it and made a hole, it is naturally the preservation of his fame. **तिर्यगायामशोभी**—As thou wilt bend lengthwise to enter that hole. **बलि**—The name of a celebrated demon. He was Virechann, the son of Prarhada, ho was very powerful and oppressed the world very much. They therefore prayed Vishnu, who descended on earth as a son of Kaśyapa and Aditi in the form of a dwarf; he assumed the dress of a mendicant and having gone to Bali prayed him to give him as much earth as he could cover three steps. Bali who was noted for his liberality unhesitatingly acceded to this, apparently simple request. But the Dwarf soon assumed a mighty form and began to measure the threo steps. The first stop covered the earth, the second, the heaven and not knowing where to place the third, he placed it on Bali's head and sent him and all his legions to Patala and allowed him to be its ruler. Vishnu is said to still guard the door in Patala. He is one of the seven Chiranjivins. of. Raghuvamśa 7. 35. **बलिप्रदिष्टां श्रियमाददानं त्रैविक्रमं पादमिवेन्द्रशत्रुः नियमन**—subduing, punishment. cf. Raghu. 9. 6. **असतां नियमनान्नराधिपोऽनुययौ**

** Verse 58.** **दशमुख** is another name of Ravana, a celebrated demon, king of Lanka and the chief of the Rakshasas. He was the son of Viśravas by Kesini and so half-brother of Kubera. He was called Paulastya as being the grandson of Pulastya. Lanka was originally occupied by Kubera but Ravana ousted him from it and made it his own capital. He had ten mouths, twenty arms and according to some four legs. (see R. 12. 85 and malti,) He is represented to have practised the most austere penance of the god Brahman for 10000 years in order to propitiate him and to have offered one head at the end of each thousand years. Thus he offered him nine of his heads and was going to offer the tenth when the god was pleased and granted him immunity from death by either god or mau. On the strength of this boon, he grew very tyrannical and oppressed all beings, his power became so great that even the gods are said to have acted as his domestic servants. He conquered almost all the gods of the day, but is said to have been imprisoned by Kartavirya for some time when he went to attack his territory. On one occasion, he tried to uplift the Kailasa moun tain when Shiva pressed it down so as to crush his fingers under it. He, therefore hymned Shiva for 2000 years so loudly that the God gave him the name Ravana and freed him from his painful position. Vishnu descended on earth as Rama, the destroyer of this demon, Ravana carried off Rama's wife while he was in a forest passing the years of his exile, and pressed her to become his wife. She remained loyal to her husband and after a hard fight Ravana with his troops of Rakshasas was hilled by Rama. **त्रिदशवनितादर्पणस्य**—on account of his possessing crystal form being made up of snow. cf. Kumar 9. 40. **विलोक्य यत्रस्पटिकस्यभित्तौ सिद्धाङ्गनाःस्वप्रतिबिम्बमारात्** & c.(gods were called Tridashas on account of their being 33 in number.) **राशीभूत**—Laugh is always considered as being white and consequently the poets imagine that this Kailasa mountain is nothing else but the laugh of Śiva collected into a heap.

** Verse 59.** **उत्पश्यामि**—look up to, expect; see post 23. **स्निग्ध**— oily, greasy. cf. post 18; Malatimadhava 10. 4. **भिन्नाञ्जन**—collyrium made of many pounded ingredients. cf. Sishupala 12. 68. **धनाः क्षणेन भिन्नाज्जन वर्णतां प्रयान्ति.** also Ratnasanhara 3. 5 **छेद**—pierce, section, cut. (cf. Kumar, 1. 49. **बलाहकच्छदविभक्तरागाम्** also Raghu. 12. 100) **हलभृत**—vide note on **लाङ्गली** verse 52. **स्तिमित**—steady (cf. Kumar. J. 87, 2. 59, **उमारूपेणतेयूयं संयमरितमितं मनः॥** Baghd.2, 22., 3. 17 ;) This is **श्रौतीपूर्णोपमालङ्कार.**

** Verse 60.** **भुजगवलयंहित्वा**—Having kept the serpent-bracelet aside (to calm the fears of his wife). Śiva is represented as wearing serpent ornaments. (Gitagovinda 6. Bhattikavya 3. 22.) **क्रिडाशैल**—Name of Kailasa, being supposed that it was created by gods for the diversion of Śiva, along with golden mountain, Mandara and Gandhamadan. cf. **कैलासः कनकाद्रिश्च मन्दरो गन्धमादनः क्रीडार्थ निर्मिताः शम्भो देवैः क्रीडादयोऽभवन् (शम्भोरहरय) दत्तहस्ता**—B. C, **दत्तः हस्ताः यस्यै**—to whom support was given. **पादचार**—going on foot **पादचारेणविहरेत्**—Might be strolling. **भङ्गी**—wave, **भक्ति**—arrangement, There for **भङ्गाभक्ति**—is the arrangements like wavy steps for **भक्ति** in this sense see post 19. Raghu. 13. 55**. अन्यत्रकालागरुदत्तपत्रा भक्तिर्भुवश्चन्दनकल्पितेन.**

** Verse 61**. **बलयकुलिशोद्धदृनोद्गीर्णतोयं–वलयानाङ्कुलिशानि तैऽद्धदृनानि तैरुद्गीर्ण तोयं येन** B. C (**कुलिश**—point **उद्घट्टन**—Striking ) that shall have ejected water by being struck by the points of bracelets (on account of friction). **यन्त्रधारा गृहत्वन्नेष्यन्ति–यन्त्रेषुधारा तासां गृहत्वं** (**कृत्रि मधारागृहत्वं**)—state of being shower-bath-room i. e, will make thee serve the purpose of shower-bath-rooms. **मोक्ष**—Release. **धर्मलब्दस्य–धर्मेलब्धस्य**—obtained (by them) in hot season. **क्रीडालीलाः**—Being engaged heart and soul in sports so as not to mind anything else. **भीषयेः–भी** substitutes **आ** for **इ** optionally and takes Atmanepada terminations in the causative if the effect is produced by the agent, here in the absence of effect it takes Parasmaipada and also augment **आ**.

** Verse 62.** **कुर्वन्कामं क्षणमुखपटप्रीतिमैरावणस्य-क्षणेमुखे पटेनयाप्रीतिस्तां** **कुर्वन्**—Verily giving delight to the Indra's elephant at the time of taking water of having a screen over the face (**ऐरावण** is another name of **ऐरावत्,** Indra's elephant), **निर्विश्**—To enjoy, governs accusative. The mountain Kailasa being your natural friend, you would be quite at home there. Natural friendship (attraction) exists betwee the following objects:—The cloud and the mountain, the lotus and the sun, the ocean and the moon, the peacock and the cloud, and the wind and the fire. The poet here gives the result that the clouds are attracted by mountains withou giving the cause for which vide appendix A. from 58—62. The poet gives the fine description of Kailas for which cf. Kumar, 9. 39. 45.

** Verse 63.** **उत्सर्ग**—which means summit here has also an implied meaning as lap, because the **यक्ष** is comparing Alaka to a woman sitting on her lover's lap. **स्रस्तगङ्गादुकूलां**—has also double meaning 1st with her garment in the shape of the Ganges dropped down. 2nd with her white garmen dropped down. **गङ्गा**—The river Ganges most sacred in India (cf. Bhartrihari 2. 10., Raghu. 2. 26, 13. 57.) vide note on verse 54. **गङ्गा** is to be taken in the second case to mean 'white' from the waters of the Ganges being white. **वः काले**—At the approach, i. e., at thy approach or rainy season. **विमाना**—has double meaning, 'as applied to Alaka having seven-storied-house' as applied to **कामिनी** 'free from pride.' The comparison is very exact and striking here, collection of clouds is compared to the hair of a woman and the shower of rain to pearl strings with which they are tied **अलका**—Name of the capital of Kubera, the lord of Yakshas on a peak of the Himalayas above the peak of Meru. cf. Infra 7.

**॥इति महाकवि श्री कालिदासविरचिते मेघदूते काव्ये पूर्वमेघः समाप्तः॥**

**———————**



**उत्तरमेघः  
————————**

 **Verse 1.** In this verse the lofty places of Alaka are compared with the cloud. So that each attribute that the cloud possesses is shown to have possessed by them, as, lightning is compared with women, rain-bow with pictures, the sound of the drum with the thunder, inward water with crystal floors and the loftiness of the cloud with the height of palaces. **अम्रंलिहाग्राः**—**अम्रंलिहन्तीत्यभ्रलिहानिशिखराणीयेषां**—whose tops reach the sky. Houses of gods and kings are called palaces. **स्निग्ध**—agreeable, charming cf. Raghu. 1.36 **स्निग्धगम्भीरोर्नेघावम्**. Uttaram 2.14, 3.28. **तैस्तौर्विशेषैः** In these particulars of. Infra 61. **तुलयितु**—to match. In the first eleven verses of this part the poet gives a lively description of Alaka. For a similar description. see Kumar 6.37—46.

** Verse 2.** **लीलाकमलं–लीलार्थं कमलं**, lotus taken out of sport. c. Kumar 684. **लीलाकमलपत्राणि गणयामास पार्वती** and Rugb. 6.13. **अनुविद्धम्**— strung or put together cf. Mrachakatika, **सौरभ्यानुविद्ध**, Madrarakhas 3. **कोपानुविद्धां चितां नाटयन्**, Kumar 3.35, **काष्ठागतस्नेहत्सानुविद्धम्** for **आननेश्रीः**—There is another reading **आननश्रीः** The beauty of the face (has become pale etc) but to keep harmony with **हस्तेः, अलके** etc. it is better to take **आननेश्रीः बाल**—young, fresh lotuses are produced in autumn, jasmine flowers in winter, lodhra flowers in spring, and Kadamba flowers in rainy seasons consequently the presence of all these flowers at all times shows the ever-presence of all seasons in Alaka on account of its being the land of celestial beings, cf. Kumar 6,37—46.

*** * Verse *(*e*)*.** This and the following verse seem to be interpolated. **उद्ग्रीवाः–उन्नता ग्रीवा येषां ते. प्रतिहततमोवृत्तयश्चरम्याश्च** appos. com. **वृत्ति**—pervasion, spreading. cf. Vikram. 2. 6 **आलोकान्तात्प्रतिहत तमोवृत्तिरासां प्रजानाम**.

*** * Verse *(*f).** **वित्तेश**—the name of Kubera, as well as of rich yakshas **यौवनादन्य द्वयी नास्ति**—cf. Kumar 6. 44. **यौवनान्तंवयोयस्मिन्॥**

** Verse 3**. **सितमणि**—may either mean crystal or moonstone either meaning being applicable here. **ज्योतिष्**—star. **छाया**—reflection. **ज्योतिषां छाया एवT कुसुमानि.** This indicates the never fading beauty of the drinking saloons cf. Kumar 6. 42. **पुष्कर**—The skin of the drum i. e. the place where it is beaten. **रतिफलं–रतिः–फलंयस्य**—having for its end sexual pleasure i. e. giving additional pleasures to sexual enjoyment, in consequence of its being taken. Mallinath takes **रतिफलं** the name of the wine. **त्वद्गगम्भीरध्वनिषु** **तत्र ध्वनिरिवगम्भीरोध्वनिर्यस्य**—Resembling thy thunder in sound cf. Kumar 6.42 **यत्रस्फटिक** **हम्येर्षु नक्तमापानभूमिषु। ज्योतिषां प्रतिबिम्बानि प्राप्नुवन्त्युपहारताम्॥**

** Verse 4.** **अमरप्रार्थिताः**—shows how beautiful they were as being even solicited by immortals. **अनुतटरुहान्तटस्यसमीपे अनुतटं** Adv. com. **अनुतटं रोहन्तीत्यनुतटरुहैः तेषां** cf. Kumar. 6. 5. **कनकसिकतामुष्टिनिक्षेपगूढैः–कनकस्यासिकतासु मुष्टिर्भिनिक्षैपणगूढैः**—concealed by putting handfuls over them in the golden sand. This play probably consisted of making heaps of sand by handfuls and concealing under one of these heaps a jewel which was discovered by another person who does not know where it is concealed. **कनकसिकता**—may either mean gold like yellow sand or sand mixed with golden particls. This and the following were the country sports played by young girls. **रासक्रीडा–गूढमणि, तुलायनम्, पिच्छकन्दूकादण्डः,** and some others. of. Kumar. 1,29 **मन्दाकेनी सेकतवेदिकाभिः साकन्दुकैः कृत्रिमपुत्रकैश्च** etc.

** Verse 5.** **अनिभृत**—Tremulous. **नीवीबन्ध**—Knot of the garment: that is worn: Malati. 2. 5. **आक्षिप्**—To pull aside, cf. Kumar, 7.58 **आग्रपादमाक्षिप्य चूर्ण**—powder of some perfume. **विफलप्रेरणाभवति—**Do not produce their desired object; ordinary lamps would be put out by throwing powders at them but as those lams consisted of light of jewels, cannot be put out by this means, hence their effort was useless. **हीमूढा**—Being at a loss what to do through shame.

** Verse 6.** **नेतृ**—Guide i. e. one who impels, urger, **आग्रभूमिः**—highest story. **आलेख्यानान्दोषमुत्पाद्य**—Defiling the pictures. **शङ्कास्पृष्टाः**—Touched by fear **उद्गार**—Mass, stream, (Here is also an implied idea of a paramour having illigal admittance to his beloved who returns from private (secret) exits after defiling her chastity and whose limbs at the time of returning are contracted through fear); **धूमोद्गार** etc. cf **माघः** 3. 61. **त्वादृशाः**—**त्वमिवदृश्यन्त इति॥**

** Verse 7.** **तन्तु जालावलम्बाः**—(**तन्तुजाल** is the not work), hanging by the net work, **त्वत्संरोधापगमविशदैः–तवसरौधस्यापगमनविशादैस्तैः**—clear by the obstruction from clouds like thee being removed. may be taken in the sense of **त्वादश ब्यालुपन्ति—**Take away, remove. **स्फुटजललवस्यन्दितश्चन्द्रकान्ताः**—moonstones oozing away visible particles of water (**चन्द्रकान्त** is supposed to ooze away under the moon) cf. Uttaram 6. 12 **द्रवतिचहिमरश्मावुद्गतेचन्द्रकान्तः** also Bhatrahari 121. Malati. 1.24.

** Verae 8.** **क्षेतुन्नशक्याः–अक्षय्याः **so also **जय्य–अक्षय्याअन्ते—भवने निधयी येषान्ते रक्तकण्ठै**—having sweet or agreeable voice (from **रञ्ज**—to please). **वैभ्राजाख्यम्, विभ्राजस्येदं वैभ्राजं तदाख्या यस्य वैभ्राजाख्यम्. वैभ्राज**—The name of the the celestial grove, another name for **चैत्ररथ,** the pleasure garden situated outside the town of Alaka, cf. Raghu. 5—60 **एको ययौ चैत्ररथप्रदेशान्सौराज्यरम्यानपराविदर्भान् उद्गीयमान**—being panegerised. cf. Rughu. 2.12. **शुश्रावकुञ्जेषुयशः स्वमुच्चे रुद्गीयमानं वनदेवताभिः बद्धालापाः**—Engaged in conversation. **निर्विशन्ति**—Enjoy. cf. Rughu. 6.34. **ज्योस्रावतोनिर्विशान्ति प्रदोषान्**—also Rughu 12.1, 4.51; 6.50; 9.36; 13. 60; 14.80; 18, 3, also Kumar. 1.29. **सार्कीडास्सन्निर्विशतीव बाल्ये॥**

** Verse 9.** **गत्योन्त्कम्प**—Flurry in walking **गन्याउत्कम्पः कनककमल** may mean gold lotuses, or gold—like yellow lotuses, as **कनकसिकता** in Verse II. 6 **पत्रछेद—** piece of tender loaf. **पत्रछेद** & **कमल** were the ear ornaments of woman in old times—**मुक्ता जाल—**perhaps means collection of pearls strung together that is worn by women in their baid of hair a chaplet. **नैश–निशिभवे** **नैश**—Nocturnal. **कामिनी**—lustful woman that goes to meet her lover of her own accord or being requested by her lover to the rendzvous generally called **अभिसारिका**.

** Verse 10.** **देव** means the god Siva who is a friend of Kubera and who is supposed to have fixed his abodo there out of affection for Kubera. **साक्षात्**—in person and not as an incarnation. **षट्पदक्यम्**—having for its string the rows of bees. **षट्पदा एव क्यायस्यतं**. cf. Kumar. 4.15. **अलिपङ्क्तिरनेक शस्त्वया गुणकृत्ये धनुषो निर्योजिता. प्रायश्चापं नवहति भयात्**—When Capid had gone to interrupt the consentration of Siva, while practising penance on the mountain Himalaya he was burnt by the god Siva by the fire of his third eye; then he was propitiated by gods; ever since Cupied has remained without body; cf. Kumar. 3.71, 72. **तपः परामर्शविवृद्धमन्यो र्भ्वूभङ्गदुष्प्रेक्ष्यमुखस्य तस्य। स्फुरन्नुदर्चिः सहसातृतीयादक्ष्णः कृशानुः किल निष्पपात॥ क्रोधम्प्रभो संहर संहरेति यावद्गिरः खेमरुतां चरन्ति। तावत्सवन्हिर्भवनेत्रजन्मा भस्मावशेषम्मदनं चकार॥** and consequently he is said to be afraid of him. **सम्भ्रूभङ्गप्रहितनयनै**—By the casting glance aocompanied by the knitting of the eye-brow. cf. Dasakumar. page 2, **कामिलक्ष्येष्ममीधैः–कामिन एव लक्ष्याणि तेषु अमोघैः**—fruitful affections towards their mark consisting of lustful persons. **तस्यारम्भ**—His work (the work of cupid). **चतुरवनिता** etc.—Amorous plays of a skilful woman serve the purpose (do the business) of the bow.

** Verse 11.** The reason why wine is given here in the list of decorations, appears to be that it produces a sort of charm as decorations do by teaching to the eyes amorous plays. **पुष्पद्विदं**—Lit. means opening of flowers, i.e. when the flowers are opened, they become fit for use **राग** comes from **रब्ज**—to dye. **रज्यतेऽनेनेतिरागः** There are four sorts of decorations. 1st That to be put on in the hair such as flowers, &c. 2nd. on the body such as ornaments, gar lands etc. 3rd. to be worn such as dress. and 4th. ointment, such as of sandle powder etc. All these here in Alaka could be procured from the desire-yielding tree alone. **कल्पवृक्षः**—One of the trees of Indra's paradise supposed to yield all desires. This was one of the fourteen valuable thinge churned out from the ocean. It is also otherwise called **मन्दर**.

** Verse 12**. **गृहानुत्तरेण**—The word **गृह** is used in Masculine in the plural only. cf. **इमेनोगृहाः** Mudrarakshasa I. **स्फठिकोपलविग्रहा गृहाः शशभृद्भित्त निरङ्कभित्तयः**; Naishadhacharita 2.74. The termination **एन** applied towords showing direction in the sense of nearness governs the accusative and the ending **अ** of the noun is dropped before it as **ग्रामन्दक्षिणेनपूर्वेणवा**—To the south or east of the village (in the vicinity). There is another reading **ग्रामादुत्तरेण—**to justify which, we must take **उत्तरेण** as an adjective qualifying **तोरणेन** meaning 'gate way which is situated to the north' **अस्मदीय**—**अस्माकमिदमस्मदीयं सुरपति वनुश्चारुणा**—which was as beautiful as the rain-bow on account of its being made of coloured crystals add being very high so as to touch as it were the cloud. **कृतकतनयः**— adopted or considered as a son, **कृतक** is also put at the end, sometimes in this sense. cf. **सोऽयं न पुत्रकृतकः पदवीमृगस्ते** (**जहाति**) Śakuntala. 4. 13. **हस्तप्राप्यस्तबकनमितः**—Bent down by the clusters which could be reached by the hand, i e., its branches were so bent down as could be reached by the hand. **स्तबक**—Bunches or clusters. cf. Bhartrihari 2. 108. **कुसुमस्तबकस्यैव**, Raghu. 18. 82. **इमां तटाशोकलताञ्चतर्न्वी स्तनाभिरामस्तकाभिनम्राम्॥**

** Verse 13.** **मरकतशिलबद्धसोपानमार्गा**—Having a stair path constructed of emarald stone. **मरकतशिला** may bo an appositional or Genitive Tatpur. compound **मरकत** **एवशिला** or **मरकतस्य शिला बौदुर्य–विदुरे भवाः–बैदूर्याः—**a kind of gem produced on Vidura mountain. cf. Kumar 7, 10. **विन्यस्तवैदूर्यशिलातलेऽस्मिन्** &c. Śishupal B. 3. 65. **स्निग्ध**—glossy. cf **पूर्वमेव** 18, 89. **सन्निकृष्टं**—There is another rending **विप्रकृष्टं** (far) but as **मानस** is situated on tho Kailasa mountain, it is better to take **सन्निकृष्टं. त्वामपिप्रेक्ष्य**—Even on seeing thee. It was the general supposition that the geese having passed 8 months elsewhere repaired to Manasa lake when the rainy season set in on account of the waters of other places being turbid in that season, while that of the Manasa lake ever remaining clear. Therefore by putting **अपि** the poet seems to mean that even when they see thee they will not think of going to Manasa as the water of the lake remained equally clear in all seasons **व्यपगतशुचः–व्यपगताशुक् येभ्यस्ते** B. C. **आभा—**To think anxiously.

** Verse 14.** **वेष्टन**—fence **मद्गोहिन्याः प्रिय इति**, i. e. **प्रिय आस्तीति**—as he is the pet of my beloved. **कातरेणचेतसा**—Frightened heart, frightened because the recollection (though it is of happy circumstance) would bring along with it sorrow (at being separated from such an object as the pet of his beloved) . **स्फुरित तडितं–स्फुरिता तडित्** **यस्य** B.c. One possessing flashing lightning. Here the cloud is compared with pleasure mountain his natural colour resembling that of the sapphire on the top lightening with plantain trees

**तमेवस्मरामि**—I am reminded of no other than love, i. e. thou appearest so very like him that I take thee to be another pleasure mountain. This is **स्मरणाख्य अलङ्कार** which is thus defined. **सदृशानुभवदन्यम्मृतिसारणमुच्यते**—remembering some familiar object by the sight of a similar object.

** Verse 15.** **रक्ताशोक**—Read Aśoka. There are two species of Aśoka, the red and the white one, as the reason of putting **रक्त** appears to be the exciting of passion. of **प्रसूनकेरशोकस्तु श्वेतोरक्तइति द्विधा। बहुसिद्धिकरः श्वेतोरक्तोऽत्रस्मरवर्धनः**। This is said, according to the convention of poets, to put forth flowers when struck by a lady with her foot decked with jingling anklets of. **असूतसद्यः कुसुमान्यशोक.........पादेन नापेक्षत सुन्दरीणां सम्पर्कमार्शिजितनूपुरेण** Kumar. 3. 26. Raghu. 8. 62. Malavlkagnimitra 8.12.16. **अकुसुमितमशोकं दोहदापेक्षया** &c. **चलकिसलय** &c. **केसर**—A kind of tree, said accordingly to the convention of poets to put forth blossoms when sprinkled by young women with mouthfuls of wine, cf, **बकुलः सीधुगण्डूषसेकात् (विकसति)**. For, the conventions of poets for different trees to blossom by different operation. cf. **पादाघाता दशोकस्तिलककुरबकौ वीक्षणालिङ्गनाभ्यां स्त्रीणां स्पर्शात्प्रियङ्गुर्विकसति बकुलः सीधुगण्डूषसेकात् मन्दारो नर्मवाक्यात्पटुमृदुहसनाच्चम्पको वक्रवाताच्चूतो गीतान्नमेरुर्विकसतिच पुरोनर्तनात्कर्णिकारः॥ वृत्ति**—hedge. **माधवी**—a spring creeper with white fragront flowers, cf. Śakuntala. 3. 7. **शोच्याचप्रियदर्शनाच मदमाक्लिष्टेयमालक्ष्यते, पत्राणामिव शोषणेन मरुता स्पृष्टा लता माधवी. एकः** and **अन्यः**—The one and the other. **दोहादपेक्षया** and **मयासह** goes with both **अशोक** and **बकुल**, I am desirous of both and each of them for either of the two with me. **दोहद**—The desire bof plants at the time of budding. It was supposed by poets that when any particular tree did not bear blossom at its proper time, it would do so by having fulfilled its longing for which see above note on **अशोक** and **केसर**.

** Verse 16**. **स्फटिक फलका–स्फटिकमया फलकायस्याः सा** B. comp. Having a crystal base. **वासयष्टि–वासार्थयष्टिः**—perchaing rod. **सुवर्णस्य विकार–सौवर्णी**—of gold. **मूलेमणिभिर्बद्धा**—constructed with emeralds at the base **अनति–प्रौढ**—not grown very old i. e. young. **शिजावलय**—bracpelets (boughs) producing jingling sound **नीलकण्ठः**—peacock—**याभध्यास्ते**—oocuies wioh. **शी**, **स्था** and **आस्** with **अधि** govern the accusative of place. cf. **पर्णशालामध्यास्य**, Ragh 1.95 **द्वितीयमाश्रममभ्यासितुसम्मयः**—Vikramorv. 5. **अयेसिंहासनमध्यास्तेवृषह** Mudra 3. **भगवत्याप्राश्निकपदमध्यासितव्य.** Nalavikayan 1. From **तन्नागारं** (12) upto the end of this verse the (**अलङ्कार**) figure of speech is (**उदात्तालङ्कार**) which is as follows. **लोकातिशयसम्पति वर्णनोदात्तमुच्यते**। **यद्वापि प्रस्तुतस्याङ्गं महता चरितं भवेत्**॥ or another definition **उदात्तं वस्तुनः सम्पन्महताञ्चोपलक्षणं** (a figure of speech which describes supermundane prosperity or an action of one that is great collaterally with the subject in hand, and this should not be mistaken for **भाविक** (or **स्वाभाविक**) **अलङ्कार** which consits in describing the past or future so vividly that it appears to be actually present, (**प्रत्यक्षा इव यद्भावाः क्रियन्ते भूतभाविनः**)

** Verse 17.** **साधु** is used here in the sense of 'clever one.' **हृदय निहितैः**—Well kept in mind, not forgotten. **लिखितवधुषौ–लिखिते वपुषी ययोः—** Drawn in form, **शङ्ख** and **पद्म** were two of the treasares of Kubera.The nine treasures were. **महापद्मश्चपद्मश्चशङ्खो मकर कच्छपौ। मुकुन्द कुन्दनीलाश्च खर्वश्चनिधयो नव॥१॥ क्षामछाया–क्षामा छायायस्य**—with faded lustre. (splendour on account of his absence. **सूर्यापाये** etc. **अर्थान्तरन्यास**—He compares himself with the sun. **कमल** is equal to daylotus **पद्म.** **अभिख्या**—splendour, beauty.

** Verse 18. शीघ्रसम्पातहेतोः–शीघ्रसम्पातएवहेतुस्तस्य**—having the object of quick descent in view. **कलमतनुताङ्गत्वा–(कलमस्यतनुरिवतनुर्यस्य तस्यभावः ताम् (अल्पशरीरतां)**—having attained small form **अल्पाल्पभासं–अत्यल्पाभाः यस्याः** of very dim lustre. **उन्मेष**—gleam, glimmer **विद्युदुन्मेषदृष्टिः–विद्युदुन्मेषएवदृष्टिः ताम्। अन्तर्भवनपतिता–भवनस्यान्तोऽन्तरभवनं तत्र पतितां खद्योतालीविलसितनिभां–खद्योतानामाल्लिः तस्य विलसितेन समानाम्। निभ** (at the end of compound only)—Resembling.

** Verse 19. श्यामा**—A kind of woman (according to Mallinath.) **यौवनमध्यस्था**—a woman in the prime of Youth. Vide. Naishadha. 3.8. Śiśupal. 8.36. according to one commentator on Bhattikavya 5.18, and 8.100. of the following description. **शीते सुखोष्णसर्वागीग्रीष्मेया सुखशीतला। तप्तकाञ्चनवर्णौभा सास्त्री श्यामेतिकथ्यते।** It may be taken also in the sense of dark woman as darkness is also a sort of agreeablo colour **शिखरिदशना**—having pointed teeth. In the science of palmistry it is regarded as an indication of her good luck and the long life of her husband. The verse runs thus, **स्निग्धाः समानरूपाः सुपङ्क्तयः शिखरिणः श्लिष्ठाः। दन्ताः भवन्तियासान्तासाम्पादेजगत्सर्वम्। ताम्बूलरसरक्तानां स्फुटभासः समोदयः। यस्याः शिखरिणो दन्ताश्चिरं जीवतितत्पतिः॥** **क्षाम** is irregular P. P. from **क्षै**. emaciated cf. post. 17. **क्षाम च्छायमभवनमधुना** etc**. चकितहरिणीप्रेक्षणा** This is the sign of her belonging to the first of four classes (viz. **पद्मिनी, शखिणी, हस्तिनी, चित्रिणी** in which writers on crotical science divide a woman. The **रतिमञ्जैरी** thus defines her:—**भवतिकमलनेत्रा नासिकाक्षुद्ररन्ध्रा अविरल कुंषयुम्मा चारुकेशीकृशाङ्गी मृदुबचनसुशीला गीतवाद्यानुरक्ता सकल तनुसुवेशा पद्मिनी पद्मगन्धा॥** also **चकितम्मृगन्दृशामे प्रान्तरक्ते चनेत्रे। निम्ननाभिः** This is the indication of exuberance of passion (lust) in crotic science **श्रोणीभारादलसगमना** of slow gait in consequence of the unwildiness of the bullocks and not through any defect therein. **स्तमाभ्यांस्तोकनम्ना** hightly bent on account of breast and not through any defect in stature. **आद्यासृष्टिः** First creation, (generally persons show their utmost skill in their first attempt that its success might pave the way in the world for them, consequently here **आद्यासृष्टिः** means creation on which the Creator has expended all his skill and not to be taken bad for want of practice. In expressions like **युवति विषय, धनविषय, विषय**—In reference to, ‘with respect to' For our poet's idea of a woman's beauty, we might well compare the following verse. Malavikagnimitra, 2. 3. **दीर्घाक्षं शरदिन्दुकान्तिवदनं बाहूनतावंसयोः सङ्क्षिप्तं पिबिडोन्नतमुरः पार्श्वे प्रमृष्टे इव॥ मध्यपाणिमितो निताम्बिजधनं पादावरालाङ्गुली छन्दोनर्तयितुर्यथैवमनसः श्लिष्टन्तथास्यावपुः॥** For a similar idea cf, Sakutala 2. 9. **चित्रे निवेश्यपरिकल्पितसत्वयोगा, रूपोच्चयेन मनसा विधिना कृतानु॥ स्त्रारत्नसृष्टिरपराप्रतिभातिसामे, धातुर्विभुत्वमनुचिन्त्यवपुश्चतस्याः॥**

** Vorse 20.** **परिमितकथां**—**परिमिता कथायस्याःसा**—One whose talk is measured. **चक्रवार्की**—Ruddy goose. The couple of ruddy goose is proverbially known to be so very fond of each other as not to bear tho slightest separation consequently separation to them would be most painful cf. Sakuntala. act. 4. **नलिनी पत्रान्तरिमपि सहचरमपश्यन्त्यातुरया चक्रवाक्यारौति** also Raghu. 3. 24. **रथाङ्गनाम्नोरिव भावबन्धनं बभूवयत् प्रेमपरस्पराश्रयं गाढीत्कण्ठाम्—(उत्कण्ठाम्—**regret caused by missing anything or person. of, **रागेष्वलब्धविषयेवेदना महतीतुया।** **संशोषणीतु मात्राणां तामुःकण्ठां विदुर्बुधाः। गाढ** from **गाह**—Unfathomable, deep. **गाढा उङ्कठा यस्यासा** cf. Mal. 1. 15. **शिशिरमथिताम् पद्मार्नीवा**—Like the frost beaten (troubled by frost) lotus. **वा** is used in the sense of **इव** here. cf. **पद्मानांशिशिरोभयम्.**

** Verse 21. प्रबलरुदितोच्छूननेत्र–प्रबलरुदिते नोच्छूने नेत्रै यस्यतत्**—B.C. having the eyes swollen by excessive weeping. (**शुन** P. P. from **श्वि**—Swollen) **भिन्नवर्णाधरोष्ठम्** (or **रौष्ठम्**)—**भिन्नवर्णोऽधरो (रौ ) ष्ठो यस्यतत्**—having the lower lip with its colour changed. **ओष्ठ** in a compound optionally substitutes **ओ** for both the vowels when the preceeding word ends in a vowel; as **बिम्ब ओष्ठ—बिम्बो (**or **बौ) ष्ठः, हस्तन्यस्तम्** placed on the (palm of the) hand. This shows the uneasy state of mind, persons (generally women) when wholly engrossed in care and anxiety place their face on the palm of their hand and think. **लम्बालकत्वादसकलव्यक्ति**— Not wholly visible by the hair falling on it cf. Vikram. 8.6., **अलङ्कसंयमनादिवलोचने** ect. The hair not being tied into braid, would fall on her face and thus cover it partially. It seems to be the custom in ancient time not to tie the hair into braid when the husband was away from home. It would be tied again on the return of the husad. **त्वदनुसरणक्लिष्टकान्तो–तवानुसरणेन क्लिष्टां कान्तिर्यस्य**—B.C. whose lustre shall have faded away by thy following him. i.e. by thy obstruction. **दैन्यम्–शोचनीयान्दशां,** Lamentable state. **नूनम्**—In all probability.

** Verse 28.** **आलोक**—Range of sight, **आलोकेतेनिपतति**—Will fall within the range of thy sight, i. e., will be seen by you. **पुरा**—Presently, soon **परा** is used to show. the past as well as future time. **सादृश्यम्**—Likeness. **भावगम्यम्**—conceiving in mind, Because she not having seen his thin form which had become so in separation must conceive it in her thought and cannot partray as seen before when he was in her company. **भर्तुःस्मरसि**—Dost thou remember the lord with regret, because **स्मृ** in the sense of remembering with reget takes the genitive of the object, in ordinary sense accusative. **भर्तारंस्मरामि—** I remember the lord. **भर्तुः स्मरामि**— I remember him with regret. The motive for regret is implied in the words **रसिके** and **प्रिया** i e. You were loved by him and you could appreciate the favour, cousequently his memory must cause sorrow in your mind. **कच्चित्** is interrogative in form and expresses some hope on the part of the speaker.

** Verse 23.** **मलिनवसने**—The wearing garment would be dirty inconsequence of my absence. In the absence of their lovers women were indifferent to these things, **मदर्गोत्राङ्कम्–मम गोत्रमङ्कंयस्मिन्** bearing the trases of my name. (**गोत्र** in the sense of name cf. Naishadha 1. 30) **विरचितपदं–विरचितानि पदानियस्य तत्–पद**—a line of a stanza. cf. Supra. 40. **त्वामुत्कण्ठाविरचित पदं मन्मुखेनेदमाह** also Malavika. 5. 2 **विरचितपदं वीरप्रीत्यासुरोपमसूरिभिः उद्गातुकामा– उच्चैर्गातुङ्कामो यस्याः**, The infinitives with **म** dropped are used with **काम** and **मनः** in the sense of 'wishing.' **नयनसलिलैः**—tears used by the sorrow on account of my separation. **सारयित्वाः**—Having put into tune. **स्वयमपिकृतां**—Though uttered by her (often) consequently not liable to be forgotten. **मुर्च्छनाम्—**Tune, intonation, the rise and fall of sounds conducting the air and harmony through the keys in a pleasing mannsr. cf. Siśupal 1. 10. **स्फुटीभवद् ग्रामविशेष मूर्च्छना.** It is thus defined. **क्रमात्स्वराणां सप्तानामारोहश्चावरोहणम् । सामूच्छेत्युच्यते ग्रामस्था एता–सप्तसप्तच (मुच्छा** and **मूर्च्छना** are used synonimously.

** Verse 24.** **विरहदिवस्यस्थापितस्यावधेः–विरहम्यदिवसात् निश्चितस्यकालस्य**—of the period determined from the day of separation i. e. she must have calculated on the first day of the separation the total number of days and then as the days rolled on, she must be deducting those days that had passed from the total number of days. **देहलीन्दत्तपुष्पैः**—Supports this interpretation. She must have heaped flowers on threshold representing the total number of days and throwing down one by one as days passed on. The flowers on the threshold representing the days to be passed and these below the days passed. (**दत्त**—Heaped or collected **परिगणनयाविन्यस्यन्ती**—counting. Lit. putting down by way of calculation such as one, two &c. **मत्सम्भोगम्**—The carnal enjoyment with me (not actual but as conceived in the mind); **हृदयनिहितारम्भम्**—May be interpreted in two ways. **हृदये निहित आरम्भोयस्य** i. e. the plan of commencement of which she had thought in mind, or **हृदयनिहिता आरम्भ (चुम्बनादयो व्यापाराः) यस्य**—The preliminary stages of which she had already begun to enjoy in the mind, **विन्यस्यन्ती** and **आस्वादयन्ती** are adjectives qualifying **सा** in the preceding stanza. **विनोदाः—कालयापनोपायाः**—Interesting occupations to while away time, cf. Sakuntala, 2. 5. **स्रिग्ववीक्षितमन्यतोऽपि** &c, **सर्व** **तत्किल मत्यरायणमहो कामी स्वतां पश्यति.**

** Verse 25.** **सव्यापाराम्** &c. There appears a break here the sentence **यथारात्रौपीडयेत्** being suppressed. But the suppression is most touching as showing the feelings of Yaksha by the very remembrance of **रात्रौ**. The word **रात्रौ** to be oxpressed along with the sentence **यथापीडयेत्** pictures to his mind the lamentable condition of his wife which he at once begins to express without finishing the first sentence, such a break we have also in Uttararama, when **यासन्ती** after repeating the lines beginning with **त्वत्जीवितं त्वमसिभेहृदयं द्वितीयं** &c. at once stops and opens quite a new subject. cf. Uttara.3. 26. **सन्धी—पारामा**—engaged in occupations like those mentioned in 2 verses 22, 23 and 24. **गुरुतर**—heavier than that at day time. **निर्विनोद्यं**—having no occupation to divert her mind to. cf. **प्रायेण**—**विनोदा**—last verse. **अलम्**—**पर्याप्तम्** completely, **सात्वीम्**—The use of **सात्वीम्** is to do away with any doubt as to how to reach another's wife at night time. **उन्निद्राम्**—**उत्सृष्टा निद्रायया** B. Sleepless. **सुख। यितुं** cf. **सखा धात्री च पितरौ मित्रदूत शुकादयः । सुखयंर्तष्टकथनसुखोपायो र्वियोगिनमिति (रत्नाकरे)** For the idea of this verse e. f. Vikram. 3. 4. **कार्यान्तारितोत्कडं दिनं मयानीतमनाते कृच्छेण। अविनोददीर्घयामा कथन्नु रात्रिर्गमयितव्या**—

** Verse G.** This and the following verse appear to be interpolations. The style and the repitition of the same ideas as occuring in verses 25 and 26. clearly show this **एक प्रख्या-एका प्रख्या यासां**— having the same resemblance, differing little. **प्रवृतिः—** Tendency, application.

** Verse H.** **अन्वेष्टव्याम्**— To be found out, as there would be no lamp there and the light of the moon would he covered by thee. **पर्यक**— generally means couch or sofa; but as we have **अवनिशयनां** in verse 25 we must take it in the more general sense of 'bed.' **अयमित नखेन करेणामोक्तव्यम्**— which is to be loosened by the hand having untrimmed nails. It seems to be the custom that the braid once tied before departure of the husband was not to be loosened till his arrival which then was to be loosened by his hand, the nails of which are untrimmed while away from home. **एकवेणी—** Single braid of hair (worn by a woman as a mark of separation from her husband). Vide verse 29. which has the same idea as this.

** Verse 26. विरहशयन**— Bed used in separation which is generally not a splendid one but one very wretched such as straw-bed &c. **सन्न्निषण्णा**— lit, planted lying. **प्राचीमूला**— corner of the rising mountain. **इच्छारति**-**इच्छया कृतानि रतानि (मध्यमपदलोपी). तामेव**— This night cannot be the same as that enjoyediu his company; but it simply means one of the like sort. **विरहमहर्तीविरहेणमहत्वेन प्रतीयमानाम्** appearing long in consequence of separation. In sorrow or when one has nothing to do, time appears long and very tedious; while on the contrary when one is happy or busily engaged the same appears very short.

 **Verse 27.** **पूर्वप्रीत्या** Thinking that they would be delighting as before **तथैवं** as before, as gone, without enjoying **खेदात्** Through disgust **पक्ष्मन्** Eyelash, cf. Raghu 19th,11, 36. **प्रबुद्धां** opened (in the case of the lotus) and (awake in the case of yaksha's wife). So also, **सप्ताम्**— closed (lotus) in sleep (yaksha's wife). **साभ्रेऽन्हवि** etc. as she will simply shut her eye being disgusted to look at the rays but as excessive anxicty will not allow her sleep, she will appear like a land growing lotus on a cloudy day which opens in the sun, and closes at night when it will be half opened in consequence of the disapearance of the sun and the absence of night.

** Verse 28.** **अधरकिसलयक्लेशिना**— distressing the tender sprout in the shape of lower lip (i. e. sprout like lowerlip; For **अधरकिसलय** cf. Sakuntata 1.21 **अधर किसलयरागः**) i, e. hot in consequence of sorrow. **विक्षिपन्तीम्**— Blowing aside by tho hot wind from the month **शुद्धस्नानात्**—Simple (without first applying fragrant oil, ointment etc.) bathing. and **शुद्धस्नान** is the sign of purity. and women in those times must have observing abstinence from things of enjoyment and leading a pure life in the absence of their husband, such as not to apply oil and form into braid the hair, put aside ornaments and costly dresses propitiating the deities for the sake of the safe returning of their husbands etc, cf. **बलिब्याकुला** in verse 22, **मलिनबसने उत्सङ्गे** in 23. **अवनिशयनां **in 25. **आद्ये बद्धा विरहदिवसेयाशिखा**— etc-29, and **सन्न्यसाभरणा** in 39, **परुषम् आङ्गडलम्बमलम्**— The hair were stiff and hanaing upto the cheeks in consequence of simple bathings. **गण्ड**— cheek. cf. Kumar. 787. Sakuntata 6.17, and Sisupal, 12.54. **उपनी** used intransitively in the sense of approach, come near." **नयनसलिलो पीडरुद्धावकाशाम्—नयनसलिलस्योत्पीडेनरुद्धोऽवकाशोयस्यास्तां**— whose entrance (scope) is obstructed by the gush of tears **अवकाश**— scope, entrance cf. (**छाया**) **शुद्धेतुदर्पणतलेप्तुलभावकाशा.** Sakuntata 7. 52. **लब्धावकशो मेममनोरथः**—5. 1, **उत्पीड**— gush, gushing flow cf. **पूरोत्पीडेतडागस्य परीवाह : प्रतिक्रिया**. Uttarrama 3. 20 also, cf. Malati: 67.

** Verse 29.** **बद्धाः** Simply tied up without forming into braid **दामहित्वा**— without the chaplet; sign of abstinence of things of enjoyment. cf. **शुद्धस्नान** last verse. **विगलितशुचा**—**विगलताशुक् यस्य**—Freed from sorrow as being again able to enjoy the company of my beloved. **मयोद्वेष्टनीयाम्**—The simple braid tied by me on the first day of separation is to be loosened by me at the end of the curse. **स्पर्श क्लिष्टम्**— giving pain at the root when touched From the (on account of being without oil). **अयमितनखैः** having untrimmed nails. This is also a mark of purity. Many sages and persons devoted to the service of Gods do not trim their nails till the period of devotion is over. **गण्डाभोभात्**— From the expanse of the cheek (from the broad cheeck) cf. Malati. 3. 8., 4. 10; 5. 11; Bh. 3. 42, 86 **भवाभोगौद्विग्नाः एकवेणीम्**— a single braid of hair (worn by a woman as a mark of separation from her husband.

** Verse 30.** **सन्न्यस्ताभरणम्**-**सन्यस्तान्याभरणानि यस्मात्**— cf, Sakuntata 6. 6. **प्रत्यादिष्टविशेषमण्डनविधिः** Vide note on **शुद्धस्नान** Verse 28. **शय्योत्सङ्गे**— In the middle of the bed cf. Kumar 1. 10. **दरीगृहोत्सङ्गनिषक्तभास; कर्णोत्सङ्ग**. Kadambari. 15. **दुःखदुःखेन**— In a quite uneasy manner. Repitition shows intensity; **प्रायः सर्वो** etc, **अर्थान्तरन्यास** vide note. Verse 1.3 **करुणावृत्ति**— state of being compassionate i.e. moved or sympathetic.**आर्द्रान्तरान्मा**— Lit one having the interior portion wet. (applicable to cloud), hence one whose heart is compassionate.

** Verse 31**. **सम्भृतस्नेहम्—सम्भृतंस्नेहं यस्मिन्**— Full of love or loving. **प्रथमविरहे**— In the first separation. First separation would be more unbearable than the subsequent ones as persons accustom themselves to it by practice and hence feel less and less, the more they are accustomed to it. **वाचाल— **talkative, boastful. **सुभगम्मन्यभाव–सुभगम्मन्यः (सुभगमात्भानं मन्यतइति**)— One who considers himself fortunate— **तस्यभावः**— The state of considering myself fortunate (**मन्य** at the end of a compound means 'considering himself to be) cf. **पण्डितम्मन्य**— One who considers himself wise. **वाचाल** etc.—Do not think that I swagger so through pride (on account of having a very high opinion of myself. **प्रत्यक्षं— **after this, substitute **भविष्यति**— will be before your eye; will be clear.

** Verse 32**. **अपाङ्गप्रसर**—The free motion of the outer corner; **प्रसर**— free motion cf. **रघुवंश.** 8. 23. **प्रतिषिद्धप्रसरेषुशत्रुषुचोन्द्रयेषुच **and 16.20. **विच्छिन्नधूमप्रसरागवाक्षाः**—also Mudra. 3.5 and Hitopadesha. 1.186. (**अपाङ्ग**—outer corner of the eye) cf. Śakuntala. 1.24. **विनयेनवारितप्रसरः मधुनः प्रत्यादेशाद्विस्मृत भ्रूविलासम्**— with the play of its eye-brows forgotten on account of the rejection of wine. cf. Infra 3.11. **मधुनयनयोर्विभ्रमादेशदक्षम्.** Wine is supposed to teach the amorous plays to the eye-brows of women. i.e. Under the influence of wind they are more amorous. **अञ्जनस्नेहशून्यम्—अञ्जनेनस्नेहस्तेन शून्यम्**—Void of the gloss of collyrium. **प्रत्यादेशात्** etc.—I have followed Malinatha in translating this line, taking **अपिच** in the sense of 'moreover,' but another meaning also appears possible and more elegant, namely, by taking **च** as connecting the first with second line and constructing the remaining portion thus: **मधुनः प्रत्यादेशादपि अविस्मृश्चुविलासं**—and with the play of its eye-brows not forgotten though wine was rejected; i.e. though she did not use wine as a sign of keeping up sorrow caused by separtion, her eyes were as amorous as before. Wine being supposed the necessary complement which gives amorous play to the eye-brows, she was so, even without it. This adds more grace to her beauty than the meaning taken by Mallinatha for **प्रत्यादेश** used in this sense. cf. supra. 51. also Sakuntala. 6.9, **इतःप्रत्यादेशात्स्वजनमनुगन्तुं व्यवसिता. उपरि स्यदिउपरि (उर्ध्वभागे) स्यन्दते (स्फुरति) इत्युपरिस्यन्दि**—Throbbing in the above region. The following are given the foretokens of the throbbings of several parts of the body—**स्यन्दान्मूश्विच्छत्रलाभं भाले पट्टं शुभं भ्रूवि। इष्टप्राप्ति दृशोरुर्ध्वमापङ्के हानिराप्नुयात्। नयन** should be taken to mean 'left eye' as left part of women and the right of men is considered best and any prognostication is to be observed on this principle. cf. **वामभागस्तु नारीणां पुंसां श्रेष्ठस्तु दक्षिणः**।

** Verse 33**. **ममेमानि मदीयास्तैः**—Belonging to me. **मुक्ताजालं**—waist-band knit together by pearls.**दैवगत्या**—By decree of fate and **हस्त सं वाहनानां**-**हस्तेन संवाहनानि**-**हस्तसंवाहनानि तेषां**—Shampoo with the hand. cf.Sakuntala, 3.18 **अङ्गे निधायकरभोरुयथासुखन्ते, संवाहयामि चरणावुतपद्मतास्रौ**॥ **सरसकदलीस्तम्भगौरः**— Yellowish like the trunk of the juicy planlain tree or the dried up one has not got gracefully yellowish colour cf **गौराचेनाक्षेप. नितान्तगौरे.** Kumar. 7.17. also Raghu. 6. 65. **गौराङ्गि गर्वं कदापि न कुर्याः**॥ The throbbing of the thigh is an indication of getting the union of the husband ere long.

** Verse 34**. **लन्धनिद्रासुखा—लब्धं निद्रा सुखंयया** B. c. By whom the pleasure of sleep is got, i.e. enjoying the pleasure of sleep. **अन्वास्य**—Seating thyself near her (Governs acc.) cf. Raghu. 2,24. **तामन्ति कन्यस्तबलि प्रदीमभन्यास्य** etc. **याममात्रं- मात्रं**—a measure whether of length, breadth, height, size, space distance or unumber. cf. also **क्षनमात्र** **निमिषमात्र**—the space of an instant. So **याममात्र—** means the space of **याम** (throd hovrs) but here **याम** appears to have been used in the indefinite sense of 'time.' It is Bah. Com. **यामःमात्रं यस्य** (a time) whose measure is **याम** i.e. for a time **सहस्र**—Wait upon (her). Though there seems no connection between the first two and the second two lines from the construction as it is, yet it appears better to take the last two lines as the reason for 'waiting,' taking इति 'understood.' That there might not be, etc. **गाढोपगूढङ्गाढञ्चतदुप**—**गूढञ्च** apps. comp. close embrace; Rughu. 13.28. **पूर्वानुभूतं कम्पोत्तरं तवोपगूढमस्मरता. सद्यः कण्ठच्युत भुजलताग्रन्थिः—सद्यः कण्ठाच्यूतो भुजलतयो ग्रन्थि र्यस्थतम्**—one in which the firm grasp of her arms round my neck will be abruptly loosened.

** Verse 35.** **तामनिलेनोत्थाप्य**—Rousing her by the wind i.e. by fanning; this shows her superiority. cf. Sakuntala. 3.18, **किंशीतलैः क्लमविनोदिभिरार्द्र वाताः सचारयामिनलिनीदलतालवृन्तैः** Because persons in deep sleep are generally roused from their sleep not by calling them out but by resorting to any of the following means, viz: By generally rubbing the feet or by fanning on the breast or by sweet song in the ear, cf. **मृदुभिमर्दनैः पादे शीतलै व्यजनैस्तनौ श्रुतौच मधुरैर्गी तौर्निद्रातोबोधयेत्प्रभुम्**। **जालक**— bud. cf. post 26. **यूथिकानि जालकानि. प्रत्यश्वस्तां**— Revived, refreshed. **विद्युद्गर्भः–विद्युद्गर्भेयस्यसः**—B. C. - Keoping it inside, i.e. not exposing it so that she may not be frightened. **स्तिमित नयनां–स्तिमिते नयने यस्याःसा**— With her eyes steady or fixed. cf. Infra. 1.35. Kumar. 2.59. **संयमस्तिमितम्मनः**, Raghu 3.17 **निवात पद्मस्तिमिते न चक्षुषा.** also U. 6,25. Steady eye on account of surprise who thou the stranger might be. **धीरः**— Looking grave in order to create confidence in her **धीरस्तनितवचने**— taken together would mean by words consisting of thy deep thundering, **धीराणिस्तमितानि तान्येववचनानि** for **धीर** in the sense of 'deep' cf. Raghu. 3.43, 59. and Uttarram. 6.17. **त्वत्सनाथ–सनाथ** here simply means ‘occupied’, . **मानिनीम्**— Proud woman, a woman possessed of self-respect cf. Kumar. 5.53.**इयम्मानिनी पिनाकपाणिं पतिमाप्तुमिच्छति**. Raghu. 13.38. **एतन्मुनेर्मानिनि माण्धकर्णेः पञ्चाप्सरोनाम विहारवारि.**

** Verse. 36**. **अविधवा–विगतोधक्षोयस्याः सा विधवा अविधवा**— one whose husband is yet living. Kalidasa is very happy and accurate in his choice of words. The very first word that he puts in the mouth of the cloud in addressing Yaksha's wife is such a one as would cheer up and support her life. When she hears himself addressed as **अविधवै** she would at once know that her husband is living and that the message imports some happy news from him, **हृदयविहितैः–हृदये निहितै**—Kept at heart i. e. not forgotton, exact **वृन्द**—Multitude, host. ef. Raghu. 12. 102. **अनुगतिमलिवृन्दैः **&c. **न्वरयति** hastens homewards to support the life of their wives which would be unbearable to them at the appearance of the clouds in the absence of their husbands. cf. post. 4. part I **प्रत्यासन्नेनभसिदयिता जीवितांलम्बनार्थ प्रोषितां**—persens gone abroad, or being on a journey, from **प्र—**away and **उषित**—lived **मन्द्रस्निग्वैर्ध्वानेभिः**—cf, Kiratarjuniya, 16.3. **पयोदनन्द्रध्यनिना धरित्रीम्** also Raghu **मन्द्रध्वनित्यजितयामतूर्यः** **अपलावण्णिमोक्षोसुकानि–अबलानांवेणीनां मोक्षे उन्मुकानि**.
