They are **अबला** (helpless) because they are to depend even for the liberation of their braid of hair on their husbands gone out vide note on No. 29. **आद्योबद्धा** etc. cf. Kumar. 2. 61. **मोक्ष्यतेसुरबन्न्दीना वेणीर्वीर्थ्यषिभूतिभिः**॥

** Verse 37**. **पवनतनयं मैथिलीव**—When Sita (Maithili) was taken away by Ravana to Lanka, Rama had sent Maruti (the son of the wind) with a token of recognition to her for cheering her up. This allusion leads us to think that the poet had, at the time of writing this poem, in his mind the message sent by Rama through Maruti to Sita. The poet also makes mention of this fact in Raghu. 12. 61, 62. **दृष्टाविचिन्विता तेन लङ्कायां राक्षसीवृता। जानकी विषवल्लीभि परीतेव महोषधिः॥६१॥ तस्येभर्तुरभिज्ञानमङ्गुलीयन्ददौकोपः। प्रत्युद्गतमिवानुष्णैस्तदानन्दाश्रुविन्दुभिः॥६२॥ उन्मुखी–उद्गतम्मुखंयस्याःसा**—With her face turned upwards (through curiosity to hear her husband's intelligence) cf. part. I 14. **अद्रेःशुङ्गंहरति पवनः किस्विदिन्युन्मुखिभिः** also Raghu 1. 39. **रथनेभि स्वनोन्मुखैःशिखण्डिनिः** and 11. 26. **उत्कण्ठीच्छ्वसितहृदया–उत्कटयीच्छ्वसितं हृदयं यस्याः साः**— with her heart heaving (swelling) through curiosity (to hear the nows). This gives the reason for hor being **उन्मुखी अस्मात्परम्**— Further than is said in verse 36. **कान्तोदन्ता**—The intelligence of the husband, cf. Raghu 12. 66. **श्रुत्वारामःप्रियोदन्तं सुहृदुपनतः**— The word **सुहृद्** is put to indicate the absence of mistatement. **सङ्गमात्किञ्चिदून**— Is little less than actual union. i. e. gives nearly the same satisfaction as the union of the husband. **सोम्यसोमन्तांर्नीनाम्** etc. is **अर्थान्तरन्यास**, vide note on verse 3. part I. In quoting the example of Maruti and Sita Yaksha also shows the chastity of his wife and the pure and necessary qualities in the cloud for & fit mossenger. They are mentioned in **रसाकट** as **ब्रह्मचारी** **बलीधीरोमायावीमानवर्जितः। धीमानुदारी निशङ्की वक्तादुतःस्त्रियाम्भवेत्**॥

** Verse 38**. **आत्मनश्चोपकर्तुं**— To make thyself blessed (happy) by obliging others. **उपकर्तुं** is generally used with the genitive. cf. Kiratarjuniya 7. 28. **सालक्ष्मीरुपकुरुते यया** **परेषां** also 8. 13 and Sisupal 20. 74. **उपकृत्य निसर्गतःपरेषामुपराधन्न हिकुर्वतें महान्त**—also **श्रहिर्ष–साधूनामुपकर्तुं लक्ष्मीं द्रष्टुं विहायसा गतुम्। न कुतूहलिकस्य मनश्चरितं च महात्मनां श्रोतुम्॥ पूर्वाभाष्यम्**— Introductory speech**, सुलभविपदाम्–सुलभा विपदीयेषान्तेषाम्म्**— For whom calamities are ever ready i. e. who are a constant pray to calamities **पूर्वाभाष्यम्** etc. is **अर्थान्तरन्यास**.

** Verse 39**. **अविरतोत्कण्ठम्**— suffering incessant pang. **तैःसङ्कल्पै र्विशति**— He unites himself with thee by the ideals known to himself i. e. he brings in his mind thy form emaciated and unites his one under the same condition with thine i. e. he brings before the eye of his mind, the ideal of thy form as suggested by his own forms and enjoys the pleasure of the union with that form Because there existed the same love of each for the other, he concludes that she must have undergone the same changes that he has undergone.

** Verse 40**. **शब्दल्येयम्–शब्देनाख्यतु योग्यम्**— could be expressed in words, i. c. which could be spoken loudly. **लोल–लालस—** cager. cf. port 61. part I Sisupal I 61; 8 46; 10 66 Raghu. 7 23; 9. 37. **श्रवणविषयमतिक्रान्त**— gone beyond the range of hearing; cf. **वृत्तनेनश्रवणविषयप्राणिणा. उत्कण्ठविरचितपदम्–उत्कण्ठयाविरचिता निपदानियस्यतत्**—The lines of which are composed in the disturbed state of mind. **पद** also may be taken to mean a sentence.' cf. part 23. P- Malavikagnimitra.5 2. Sakuntala, 5. 15.

** Verse 41.** There are four remedres of amusing for persons separated from their beloveds. They are:—**सदृश्यप्रतिकृतिलस्वप्नदर्शन तदङ्गस्पर्श**. i. e. looking at similar object, at her picture drawn, seeing her in dream, or the touch of the object. It is thus described in **गुण्णपताकाः–वियोगावस्थासु प्रियजनसदृक्षानुभवनं तताश्चित्रं कर्मस्वप्नसमये दर्शनमपितन्दगस्पृष्टानामुपगतवतांस्पशर्नमपि प्रतीकारोऽनङ्गव्यश्चितमनसाङ्कोनिगदितः**॥ The poet gives them in order in verses 41, 42, and 44. **श्याम— **Priyangu creeper. The stature of a woman is generally composed to the creeper. cf. Malavikagnimitra. 2.7 **कृत्याश्यामाविटपसदृशं स्रस्तमुक्तन्द्वितीयम्**. Hence it must have come to apply to a beautiful woman. cf. part 21 P. **चकितहरिणी प्रेक्षणे दृष्टियातम्**—The glance in frightened deer.The glances of a woman are usually compared to the look of a deer or a frightened deer. cf. Mrachakatika 1. 17. **व्याधानुसारचकिताहरणीबयासि**. also Raghu. 18. 18. **मार्गे मृगेक्षिणि दृष्टिपातं कुरुष्व** Mallinath's taking **पात** to mean **प्रभा** appears unnecessary, it simply means, throwing, **दृष्टिपात**— Throwing of the glance. **वक्रच्छायां शशिनि–छाया** is equal te beauty. The face of a woman is compared to the moon **हन्त**— is here used showing grief, in the sense of oh, alas; besides it is used in the other senses, as joy compassion or pity, as an introductory particle. **चण्डि**— Oh. thou hot tempered one! (used in good sense) Yaksha uses the word **‘चण्डि’** to show that she being hot tempered one, might get angry even for comparing these objects to her and by putting ‘**चण्डि’** he requests her as it were not to do so. cf. Raghu, 8. 59. **कलमन्यभृतासुभाषितं कलहंसीषुमदालसङ्गतम् पृषतीषू विलोल मीक्षितं पवनाघूतलर्ताम्प्तुविभ्रमाः**॥ for the idea of this verse.

** Verse 42**. **प्रणयकुपितां–प्रणयेनकुपितां**— Eeigning anger through excessive love. **धातुराग–धातव एवरागाः** (**धातु** red mineral **राग** colour)—colours consisting of red minerals **आत्मानं यावात्ते चरणपतितं कर्तुमिच्छामि** while I try to draw myself also in the picture as fallen prostrate at thy feet **कृतान्त**— Generally god of death. It also means 'fate in which sense it is used here, i. e. who can bring out the end. For the idea of the verse compare Dushyanta's lamentation over the picture of Sakuntala that was drawn by him. Ś. 6. 22 **प्रजागरान्खिलीभूतस्तस्याः स्पप्नेसमागमः। बाप्यस्तुनददात्येतान्द्रष्टुञ्चित्रगतानपि॥** 2nd remedy of amusement of love-lorn person, see; note, II, 41.

** Verse 43.** **आकाशप्रहितभुञ्जं–आकाशेप्रणिहितौ भुजौयेन**—B. C.—With arms stretched out in the vacuum (for embracingthec) **स्वप्नसन्दर्शन–सुप्तस्यविज्ञानं स्वप्नः तत्रसन्दर्शनम्**— conciousness in slcep. **स्थलोदेवता**— Silvan deity. **नखलुन**— Favourite expression of Kalidasa. of putting two negatives to show dead certainty cf. Malavika. 1. II. **नचनपरिचितो** &c. also Sakuntala 3. 8. **नेयं नवक्ष्यति. मुक्तास्थूला तरुकिसलयेष्वश्रुलेशाःपतन्ति**— The drops of tears as big as pearls will fall on the tender leaves (sprouts) cf trees. The natural reason why yaksha says that the drops will fall on the leaves of trees appears to be that the drops when they fall on tender leaves assume the form of pearls and their magnitude could be very easily calculated in order to justify his remark **मुक्तास्थूला** he seems to use the expression. But Mallinath also attaches some reason from palmistry that in order to avoid the prediction os Yaksha's death if they were to fall on the ground he uses the expression **तरुकिसलेषु** by giving the following quotation **महात्मगुरुदेवानाशुपातःक्षितौयदि। देशभ्रंशोमहादुःखं नरणं च भवेद्धुवम्।** and saying. **क्षितौदेवताश्रुपात निषेधनाद्यक्षस्य मरणाभावसूचनार्थं तरुकिसलयेषु पतन्तीत्युक्तम्.** This is the 3rd remedy of amusement in separation. Vide note Verse 41. P. II. cf. with this, Raghu. 8.70 **विलपन्निति कौसलाधिपः, करुणार्धग्रथितं प्रियां प्रति। अकरोत्पृथिवीरुहान विप्लुतशाखारसबाष्प दुर्दिनान्.**

** Verse 44.** **किसलयपुट**— The fold of the sprouts i.e. the cup sprouts cf. R. 9.68. **तस्यकर्कशविहारसम्भवं स्वेदमाननविलग्नजालकम्। आचचाम सतुषारशीकरो भिन्नपल्लवपुटोवनानिलः**॥ also Malavikagnimitra 8 9 **स्रुति**— Flow. cf. Kumar. 16. **पदं तुषारं स्रुतिधौतरं**— to also. Ragu.16.44

**बाष्पवृष्टि हिमस्स्रुति हैमवर्ती ससर्ज.** Kumar 1. 9. **स्रुतक्षीरतया प्रसूतोगन्धः सुरभी करोति दक्षिणेन प्रवृत्ताः**—which began to move (set out) in the southern direction. The direction or rout followed to go to a particular place also becomes an instrument. cf. Vikramorvashi. I. **कतभेनदिग्भोगन गतसजाल्मः किल**— perchance, probably (showing probability). 4th remedy. see note verse 4.1.

** Verse 45. दीर्घयामा-दीर्घायामायस्याः सा**—The watches of which are long, actually they were not longer or shorter than as they were previously, but in anxiety and sorrow, the man feels the days long and tedious which on the contrary in happiness appear shorter cf. post. Verse 26. P. II. **नीतारात्रिःक्षण इव** etc. **सर्वास्वस्थासु**— in all conditions. **मन्दमन्दातपं—मन्दप्रकारेण (प्रकारे गुणवचनस्य)** repetetion shows 'very little' **आतप—सन्तप**— giving trouble. **चटुलनयने**— Oh thou one having eyes tremulous (through fear on hearing this account.) **दुर्लभप्रार्थनं भेचेतः—दुर्लभा प्रार्थना यस्य तथाभूतं**— whose desired object is unobtainable, cf. Vikramorvashi. 2. **मयाखलुदुर्लम प्रार्थितयाकथमात्मा विनोदयितव्यः** and 26. **असुलभ प्रार्थनादुर्निवारं मे मनः**

 **Verse 46. बहुविगणयन्** - calculating much (upon the future happiness at the end of the curse) **आत्मानमान्ननावलम्बे**— I cheer up myself by myself i.e. there being nobody to give me courage, I take heart myself. **ननु (आमन्त्रणे)**— May be as avocative particle **कस्यान्यन्तं सुखमुपनतं** etc. **अर्थान्तरन्यास** very commom expression. cf. Raghu 14. 65. **किंवातवात्यन्तवियोगमधि हतजीविते**. Munusmrite. **अत्यन्त सुखमश्नुते** H. 4. 73. **नायमत्यन्तवासलाभ्यते येन केनचित्**— Vikramor vaśi. 43. **साचात्यन्तमदर्शनं नयनयोर्याता. दशा**—condition of men. **नेमि**—Ring or felly of awheel, cf. Raghu 1. 39, 17. **रथनेमिस्वनोन्मुखैः, नेमिवृत्तयः**॥

** Verse 47.** **शापान्तों मे भुजगशयनादुत्थिते शार्ङ्गपाणौ (भबिष्यति)**—my curse will end when Vishnu will rise from His serpent bed. Now Vishnu is supposed to go to bed consisting of the serpent (hence His epithet **शेषशायि**) on the 11th day of **आषाढ** and rise again on the 12th of **कार्तिक.** of **मनुस्मृतिः**—**सुप्ते न्वायिजगन्नाये जगत्सुप्तं भवेदिदम्। विबुद्धं त्वयि बुध्येतःसर्वचराचर** with this prayer he is to be sent to bed on 11th day of **आषाढ** and is to be roused on 12th of **कार्तिक** by the following verses: **ब्रर्ह्मेद्ररुद्राग्नि कुबेरसूर्य सोमादिभिर्वन्दित वन्दनीयः। बुध्यस्वदेवेशजगन्निवास मन्त्रप्रभावेन सुखेन देव॥ इयं च द्वादशीदेव प्रबोधार्थ निर्मिता॥ त्वयैव सर्वलोकानां हितार्थ शेषशायिना॥ उत्तिष्ठोतिष्ठ गोविन्द त्यजनिद्रां जगत्पते। त्वयिसुप्ते जगःसुप्तमुत्थितेचोत्थितञ्जगत्॥** and this seems to be the origin of what is observed as **चातुर्मास** in the Deccan. During these four months great religious ceremonies are observed by almost all classes of Hindus especially by Brahamanas. **शार्ङ्ग** is the general name for a ‘bow' or ‘the special bow of Vishnu.' **लोचने मीलयित्वा**—Shutting they eyes i.e, silently, without complaining taking courage. cf. Marathi, expression used in the same sense. **डोळे झाकून’** **विरहगुणितम्**—accumalated in separation (on account of nonenjoyment), There is another reading **विरहगणित** which is equally good meaning 'calculated in separation as having no other occupation;' lovelorn persons will naturally be counting the enjoyment to be enjoyed in future. **तन्तमाभिलाषम्**—those various enjoyments thought of in mind in separation. **निवेक्ष्यावः**—We shall enjoy. cf. Raghu 6.34. **ज्योत्सावतीनिर्विशति प्रदोषान्** also. 12.1; 4. 51; 6. 50. Kumar 1.29.**परिणतशरच्चन्द्रिकासुक्ष्यासु**—In nights having full-grown moonlights. cf. Bhatrihari, 3,4C. **वयं पुण्यारण्येपरिणतशरच्चन्द्र किरणैस्त्रियामां नेक्ष्यामः**।

** Verse 48.** **कण्लग्ना**—**कण्ठेलग्ना**—Throwing thy arms round the neck so as to have no possibility of my being away and propitiating any other body. **किमपि**—on some indescribable account. **सस्वरं**—**स्वरोणसहितं यथा तथां** adv. loudly. **सान्तरहासं**—Lauging inwardly (in the sleeves), secret or suppressed laugh, hence with a gentle smile, **कितव**—cheat, rogue, (used fondly).

** Verse 49**. **एतस्मादभिज्ञानदानात्**—(**दान**—receiving). After receiving the token of recognition given in the preceding verse. **कौलीन**—Public scandal, something heard from horesay. **मध्यविश्वासिनी माभूः**—Do not be distrustful with respect to me i.e. (as to whether I am alive or dead) by hearing public report. For they will be saying any thing and everything they like. **स्नेहानाहुः किमपि बिरहे ध्वंसेनः**—construc—**स्नेहान्विरहे ध्वसिन आहुस्तत्किमपि**—They say that affections die away in separation that is something (not worth minding) Thou needst not mind that hackneyed maxim. **किन्तुतेऽभोगादिष्टे वस्तुन्युपचितरसाः प्रेमराशीभवन्ति**—But they with their taste for the desired object, accumulated turn out into a heap of affection i.e. grow more and more in separation. **अर्थान्तरन्यास.**

** Verse 50**. **आश्वास्य**—cheering up. cf. Vikram. 3. **तदासङ्कीर्तनैनाश्वासयाम्यात्मानम्.** Raghu 14.58. **आश्वास्यरामावरजासर्ती ताम्** etc. **त्रिनयनवृवोत्खातकूटात्**—cf. 52. P. I. **शुभ्रत्रिनयनवृषोत्खातपङ्को पमेयां शीभाम्. साभिज्ञान प्रहितकुशलैः**—**साभिज्ञानं यथतथा प्रेषितं कुशलं येषु**—In which the message of her doing well is sent along with some mark of recognition. **प्रातः कुन्द प्रसवशिथिलम्**—(**प्रसव**—flowers) The flowers of Kunda are very loose and in a conditon to drop down from the stems in the morning. Kunda flower appears to be one of the favourite flowers of the poet also Śakuntala. 519. **भ्रमरइव विभाते कुन्दमन्तस्तुषारं परिभोक्तुं नैवशक्तोपिहातुम्.**

** Verse 51**. **कच्चित्** is used in asking questions. **सोम्य** is often used in tho sense of "good sir, gentle sir," cf. Raghu 14.44, and 59 **प्रीतोस्मि ते सौम्यचिरायजीव** Kumar. 4. 35. Mal. 9. 25. Post. P. I.49. P. II. 23. **व्यवसितम्**—Undertaken, consented to do. **प्रत्यादेशान्नखलु भवतो धीरताङ्कल्पयामि**—**प्रत्यादेशा ते धीरता** (**जाता**) **इतिनकल्पयामि** (**समर्थये**)—I do not think that thy gravity results from refusal i. e. I do not think that because thou art grave (silent) thou refusest to do my business. cf Sakuntala 6.9 **प्रत्यादेशात्स्वजनमनुगतुं व्यवसिताम्॥ निःशब्दोऽवि**—Though silent i. e. not giving a reply in the shape of thundering. **याचित**—When thou art asked (by the chataka bird which is said to drink no other than the rain-water, and which in consequence is eagerly longing for rain, cf. Bhartrihari. 2.121. **सूक्ष्माएव पतन्ति चातकमुखे द्वित्राः पयो बिन्दवः**, also, Raghu. 5.17. **शरद्धनं नार्दति चातकोऽपि॥ प्रत्युक्तंहि प्रणयिषु सतामीप्सितार्थक्रियैव**—Because the reply of the good to the supplicant is the execution of the business. i.c.they never wait to give a reply but at once begin to fulfil the request of the mendicant. cf. Vikramorvashi.4.15. **स्वार्थात् सतां गुरुतरा प्रणयिक्रियैव** (It is **अर्थान्तरन्यास**) also. **गर्जतिशरदिनवर्षति वर्षाति वर्षासु निस्वनोमेघः नीचोवदति न कुरुते न वदति सुजनः करोत्येव॥**

** Verse 52.** **आत्मनोनुचित्**— Fit, not lowering they dignity **विधुंर**—love-lorn, helpless. cf. Virkramorvashi. 4.20, **मयिच विधुरे भावः कान्ता प्रवृत्ति पराङ्मुखः** Siśupal. 6. 29. **विधुरबन्धुरबन्धुरमैक्षतमय्यनुक्रोश बुद्ध्या**—Through compassionate feeling towards me (words implying pity or compassion govern the Locative.) cf. 5.3. **भगवन्कामदेवनतेमय्यनुक्रोशः सम्भृतश्रीः**—full of (or posses. sed of) beauty. **विद्युताविप्रयोग**—words implying ‘separation from' are usually construed with the instrumental. cf. Vikram. 4. **अयमेकपदेतया वियोग उपगतः**—The conclusion here appears so natural on account of the devout prayer of Yaksha in the concluding verse being qvite compatible with his wishes that it would be folly to suppose that the three verses interpolated hereafter are by the same author and besides it would spoil the whole charm of the conclusion.

**——————**

**APPENDIX**

**<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1722927434758.png"/>**

**IMPORTANT NOTICEABLE POINTS IN THE POEM.**

 1. Theory of evaporation and rainfall poetically described in verses—5, 12, 13, 17, 19, 20, 22, 26, and 61. (Part 1.)

 For this the following short account might be of some use.

 Clouds are masses of vapour, condensed into little drops or vesicles of extreme minuteness like fogs. There is no difference of kind between fogs and clouds. Fogs are clouds resting on ground. To a person enveloped in it a cloud on a mountain appears like a fog. They always result from the condensation of vapour which rises from the earth. The minute drops or vesicles which uniting together form a cloud are supposed to be formed of an infinitely minute hollow lubbles like soap bubbles filled with air which are hotter than the surrounding air. So these vesicles float in the air like so many small balloons. Others again suppose that clouds and fogs consist of extremely minute droplets of water which are retained in the atmosphere by the ascensional force of currents of hot air, just as light powders are raised by the wind; ordinarily, clouds do not appear to descend but this absence of downward motion is only apparent. In fact, clouds do usually fall slowly but then the lower part is continually dissipated on coming in contact with lower and more heated layers, at the same time the upper part is always increasing from the condensation of new vapours so that from these two actions, clouds appear to retain the same height.

 As for the formation of clouds there are many canses which concur in their formation. The usual cause of the formation of clouds is the ascent, into higher regions of the atmosphere, of air laden with aqueous vapour, it. thereby expands; being under diminished pressure and in consequence of this expansion it is cooled and this cooling produces a condensation of vapour. Hence it is that high mountains, stopping the currents of air and forcing them to rise, are an abundant source of rain. If the air is dry its temperature would be one degree lower for every 1000 feet. The case is different with moist air. For when the air has ascended so high that its temperature has fallen to dew-point,aqueous vapour is condensed and in consequence of this, heat is liberated. When the dew point is thus attained and the air is so laden with aqneous vapour that it cannot take up any more of it at that temperature, the cooling due to the ascent and expansion of air causes rain.

 When the individual vapour vesicles become larger and heavier by the constant condensation of aqueous vapour and when finally individual vesicles unite, they form regular rops which fall as rain.

** 2: Figures of speech, verses :—**

\(a\) **अर्थान्तरन्यास**, (Part 1) 3, 5, 6, 10, 17, 20, 28, 38, 41, 53. (Part 2) 17, 24, 36, 37, 38, 46, 49, and 51.  
(b) **विषमांलकार** verse 5.  
(c) **प्रेयालङ्कार** verse 6-11.  
(d) **भाविकालङ्कार** (c).  
(e) **श्रौतीपूर्णोपमालङ्कार** 54.  
(f) **स्मरणाख्यालङ्कार** 14 (II)  
( g ) **उदात्तालङ्कार.** 12—15.

** 3, Cloud compared to :—**

\(a\) The breast of the earth. (b) To a lover, 28, 29 and 40. (c) to Vishnu, 46. (d) to a gallant II. 6. (e) to a pleasure mountain II. 14.

** 4. Clouds lineage. 6.**

** 5. Anxious look at the cloud of wives of persons away from home through confidence of their return. 8**.

** 6. Supposed good omens for a happy and unobstructed journey. 9—11.**

** 7. Historical reference to Kalidasás date according to Mallinath's explanation. 14.**

** 8. Land ejecting peculiar fragrance :—**

\(a\) After it is ploughed 16. (6) After it is burnt 21. (c) After the 1st. rain fall. 42.

** 9. Reversed appearance falling at the foot of a mountain. 19.**

** 10. River compared to woman. 28,29.**

11\. Discription of a country at the approach of rainy season. 23.

12\. Discriptive and Imaginative verses. 18,23, 25,26,61.

13\. Beautiful discription of Ujjayini 30—32 and three interpolated verses.

14\. Discription of Mahakala. 33—36.

15\. Skanda's history. 43—44.

16\. Historical reference of Rantideva. 45, **कुरू** 48.

17\. Discription of Himalaya. 52—57.

18\. Discription of Himalaya Kailasa. 58—62.

19\. Discription of Himalaya Alaka. 1—11. & 2 interpolated verses.

20\. Discription of Himalaya Yakshas house. 12—17, P. I. 7.

21\. Ideal of woman's beauty. 19.

22\. Discription of the condition of his wife 19—21 (in general of a woman separated from a lover.)

23\. How she will be found by the cloud, 22,24,30.
